"Oh, my children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, due to its completion it has come to an end. And because of its explanations and clarifications, it seems to me that I fulfill what I promised to you with this treatise, which deals with surgery by hand."
"Since the operation by hand is almost entirely lost in our region and time, to such an extent that the science of it is completely forgotten, and only a few descriptions remain in the books of the Ancients, which are now changed hands and have become obsolete due to their errors and mistakes. Therefore, its intentions are closed and its power weakened."
"And it seems to me that I should revive this with an ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and clarification and abbreviation; and so that it comes with the forms of cautery tools and other instruments of the work, both for addition to the clarification and preparation of it, which is necessary."
"However, the reason why there is no good craftsman with his own hand in our time is because the art of medicine is long, and its practitioner must be well-trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, which includes knowing the joints of the limbs, their shapes, connections, separations, knowledge of bones, nerves, and muscles, their numbers, arrangements, and locations of pulsating veins and quiet ones."
"And therefore Hippocrates says that 'in the name but not in deed', meaning that he excelled more in writing than in surgery."
"But we have already said at the beginning of this book that anyone who does not know what we have said about anatomy will surely fall into error and cause many deaths. For I have seen too many such cases, where some are formed in this science but depart from it without knowledge or experience."
"For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who operated on an abscess in a woman's neck, cutting some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed out and the woman died immediately."
"And I saw another doctor who tried to remove a stone from a man's bladder that had become very enlarged. He came and removed that stone along with a piece of the bladder wall, causing the man to die three days later."
"And I had already predicted that this would happen, for I saw that because of the size of the stone and the disposition of the illness, he would certainly die."
"And I saw another doctor who was paid by one of our dukes to perform surgery. This doctor approached a blacksmith with a dislocated hip fracture. However, due to his ignorance, he reduced the dislocation improperly using pillows and wedges with great force, not allowing the hip joint any room to breathe."
"And he then relocated the limb according to his desires, but when he reduced it, he immediately released it and left it alone for some days. Then he commanded that the bandages be removed, and thus he caused the hip joint and thigh to become inflamed, leading to ruin."
"And I was called to him, and I prepared to release the bandages. Then he became calm and free from his pains."
"But nevertheless, corruption had already established itself in the limb, so that I could not prevent it. And corruption continued to spread throughout the limb until the patient died."
"And I saw another doctor who perforated a cancerous abscess. The wound became ulcerated after some days, and the malignancy of it was greatly magnified in the patient."
"This is because cancerous tumors are caused by black bile. Therefore, it is not necessary to cauterize them completely with hot iron, but rather to operate on the limb that suffers from it so that it may be hosted."
"And therefore, my sons, it is necessary for you to divide surgery into two parts: one part concerns operations associated with health, and the other involves works in which there is great danger in most dispositions."
"And I have already stated this in every place throughout this book where there is mention of operations involving error and danger. Therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against that and leave it alone, so that foolish people may not find an opportunity to speak and bring dishonor upon you."
"Therefore, take up your arms with diligence and protection from God, and treat your patients with skillfulness and steadfastness."
"And follow the best path through the grace of God, losing your way to health and success. Leave behind difficult diseases that are hard to cure, and put aside your fears, so that you may remain steadfast in your faith and name: for it is more glorious for you, both here on earth and afterwards, with regard to your sanctity."
"Just as I have stated in some previous discourses:" "Do not treat an illness badly, lest you be named a bad doctor."
"And I have already divided this book into three sections according to its contents."
"Begin the division of the book, starting with the first part." "The first chapter is concerned with the following topics within the first section: the shape of instruments and the forms of cauterizing irons, and what is necessary for surgery."
"Division of the second part" "The second chapter is about cautery and perforation, cupping glasses, ligatures, extraction of arrows and similar objects, all ordered according to the forms of instruments."
"The third chapter is about reduction and relocation, and treatment of torsion and similar conditions. This chapter is organized according to the shape of instruments."
"It is necessary for me to speak about the qualities of those things that are useful and harmful in cauterization, and in what condition cautery is prohibited."
"Therefore, I say that the discussion about the qualities of what is useful and harmful in cautery is long and detailed, subtle through science, and secretively concealed. Many wise men have spoken at length about this topic, and they disagree with each other on it. It suffices me to mention a little of their discussions, for fear of prolonging."
"And therefore I say that cautery generally benefits all conditions universally, whether they are material or immaterial, except for two conditions which are without matter."
"In the case of a dry and hot complexion with matter that is out of order; for some say that cautery is beneficial for this, while others say the opposite, that cautery is not suitable for an illness that is due to heat and dryness, since fire has qualities of heat and dryness, and it is inappropriate for an illness of a hot and dry nature with matter that is cauterized and dry to be healed in this way."
"And he who says the opposite of that, namely that cautery is beneficial in all hot and dry illnesses that occur in human bodies, argues that when you compare the body of man and its humidity to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man very similar."
"I say according to the speech of him, that I have experienced this many times myself."
"However, it is not necessary for me to speak further about this, since the matter has already been thoroughly examined and discussed in the chapter on cautery. And having known the diversity of complexions among men, the disposition of illnesses within them, their causes, accidents, and duration of time, [I have covered] everything."
"But in other complexions, there is no doubt, and especially in hot and humid illnesses, for all physicians agree about them, and they are not in disagreement about the benefit of cautery in those cases."
"And know, my son, that the secret of curing with cautery by fire and its effectiveness lies in cautery with burning medicine. For fire is simple, whose action does not extend beyond the member that is cauterized, and it does not harm any other member adjacent to it except with a slight injury."
"But the action of burning medicine extends to those members that are burned by it, and sometimes it causes illness in them that is difficult to cure, and sometimes it even causes death."
"But fire, because of its subtlety and its good substance, does not do anything except superfluous. And we know this through experience and the length of service in study with the art concerning the truth of causes; therefore I am excused from lengthy speech. And if it were not that my book is not yet read in this place, I would conceal from you in this pause a secret about fire, namely the quality of its operation on bodies and its expulsive power by which it expels illnesses, demonstrated with philosophical proof, which would clarify your thoughts."
"And know, my son, that they disagree about the time when it is convenient to perform cautery, and they consider the best time to be in spring."
"And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because the harm that may occur by chance is submerged in the benefit of what is attracted by the cautery. And especially if the cautery is performed for pains or necessary operations, such as fistulas, which do not tolerate delay because it is feared that greater malice will come, which is worse than a slight injury entering through time."
"And do not think about this, my son, for only the common people and foolish physicians estimate that. For those illnesses that are cured by cautery have a remedy at all times, but they postpone it."
"And the reason is not as they imagine it to be because cautery is only a substitute for medicine that alters complexion and dries out humidity, which are the cause of pain."
"But nevertheless, cautery is superfluous over medicine because of its volatility and virtue of its operation and the greatness of its heat."
"But it is possible that the illness returns at some time in the future, depending on the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness, and the virtue of cautery, and what is prepared in the body from the aggregation of its superfluities, and what is received by it in its acquisition through foods and similar causes. But the illness in which cautery is administered should be a subtle one in a member with few superfluities and humidity; thus, cautery for toothache and similar ones does not usually return, but this occurs rarely."
"And also the common saying is that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and this saying is truer than they understand it to be because they believe that nothing else profits besides cautery."
"But the reason is contrary to this; and the intention that cautery is the last resort of medicine only applies when other methods of cure are tried for certain illnesses, and those medicines do not help, and therefore cautery is administered at the end of the cause, and it profits there." "And from now on understand that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention understood by the common people and many foolish physicians."
"And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this because of anything other than the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance."
"And they said that the place of cautery does not matter, which is not absolutely true because I have seen and proven that this is only the case in some bodies without others, and cautery with it is good and better than with iron, as they said. But when you perform cautery with fire using gold, it is not declared to you because it depends on the quantity of heat that you want from the roughness of the gold, and because it prepares to receive friction; and if you adjust the ignition, the gold will melt in the fire, and some laminae may fall into the fire due to the occupation of the artisan."
"And for that reason, cautery with iron should be performed more gently and more moderately according to the virtue of its operation."
"And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head within the chapters so that later you can find what you want from them."
"The first chapter."
"This cautery helps against humidity and coldness in the serous accident caused by these two causes, such as soda and multitude of fluxes called coriza from the head to the parts of the eyebrows and ears flowing, and multitude of sleep, and toothache and jaw pain, and generally all illnesses that come from coldness, such as paralysis, sodomitisal diseases, and apoplexy, and similar ones in these illnesses."
"The form of this cautery is as follows: first, command the patient to be purged with laxative medicine clarifying the head for three or four nights, according to what the virtue of the illness and the age of the patient and his habit require."
"And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then perform the cautery between your hands over a carpeted bench and have him place his hands on his knees."
"And then place the edge of your palm just above the bridge of the nose between his eyebrows." "But however, when your little finger reaches the middle location, mark that spot with a tent and then ignite the olive oil cautery of which this is the form:"
"And then place that over the spot marked with a tent in such a way that it descends while your hand is gradually constrained and you turn it."
"And then lift your hand gently and observe the spot. If you see any amount of bone already exposed on the head, as much as the amount of a grain of barley, then raise your hand again, and if not, turn your hand with that iron, but another one if it has cooled, until you see what I have said to you."
"Then take some salt and dissolve it on that spot; let it sit for three days."
"And pause over the burn wound at its edges, letting it sit until the fire's skin is destroyed." "And then treat the spot with tetrafarmacon cream until it heals."
"And they said that when the plague is opened, the arm should be bandaged more tightly, for it is better and more beneficial in this way."
"And some of them said that the vein should be cauterized near to the bone, and the cautery should be held until some part of the bone's head is adhered."
"And then scrape off what has adhered to the bone, and then it shall be healed."
"And others said that when the cautery reaches the end, it should be pressed onto the bone with great force until the bone cracks, and this is the small form of alphecati." "And they believe that from that spot the vapors of the head expire."
"And let the opened plague be held for a long time, and then it shall be healed until it is consolidated."
"But I have not seen these two kinds of cauteries in any man, except some because of fear; and leave that, it seems to me, better is with health when it is; for the head is softened by solution of continuity from this same as we have testified in the other members, and more so when the head of the disease is very strong."
"And the first kind of cautery is safer and better in my opinion; and that way with that work is healthier."
"Chapter Seven:"
"Of the cautery for the head."
"When severe and prolonged headache occurs in a patient who uses various remedies such as ointments, poultices, bandages, emplasters, powders, cataplasms, liniments, etc., especially if cautery has been applied without improvement, consider whether the patient's head is constitutionally strong. If it is not hot and dry but rather moist and cold, then cauterize again with another cautery." "He cauterized that over the horn of his head with a cautery until the flesh was parted." "Cut the flesh until you see the amount of bone we mentioned and cauterize him with a cautery at the last part of the head where it is called 'the vessel,' which is also where cupping is performed." "And be gentle in this, and do not expose the bone, for this disease causes less pain than all other cauteries of the head."
"And this cautery should be applied in its proper place, for it is necessary to use a more subtle cautery on the horns of the head and the occupit than that used on the middle part of the head. This is its form."
"Chapter Three."
"Of the cauterization of non-ancient migraine."
"When severe pain occurs suddenly in the part of the head, or there is persistent pain extending to the ear, evacuate with medicines that cleanse the head and administer the other treatment mentioned earlier for this disease. But if it does not help, cauterization is then performed in two ways: either cauterization with a medicine that causes burning, or with iron."
"The cautery with a burning medicine is made as follows: Take a dollop of aloe and scrape it clean, then remove both its ends." "And then carefully cut the location of the pain in the temple with a sharp lancet until you see the bone beneath the flesh, but do not expose it."
"Then press over it with a hot compress for a moderate constriction and leave it there for the space of three hours. Then remove it and take away the aloe and let the wound lie open for two or three days, then apply a poultice of bread dough around it until the area becomes dry."
"And then treat it with an ointment until it is healed."
"If you wish, do this with some burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines."
"The cauterization with iron according to this method is as follows:"
"And it is called 'closed nails', for its head is shaped like a nail with some curvature, and there is a small prominence in the middle of it."
"And apply pressure onto the painful spot, hold your hand steady — so that the heat of the iron is not wasted — and slowly move it back and forth with speed."
"And if the amount of heat absorbed by the skin is as much as its magnitude, lift your hand up so that the artery that is left is not burned, so that blood does not flow."
"And apply cotton soaked in saltwater onto the spot and leave it there for three days; and then apply warm compress with its edge and cure it with ointment until it heals."
"And if you wish, cauterize the extremity of the catheter according to cautery and beware of cutting into an artery in this migraine that is not ancient."
"Chapter Four."
"On the Cautery Treatment of Ancient Migraine."
"When you treat migraine with what we have said about the previous cure and what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, but the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the catheter within until it becomes white. Because it signifies onto the spot of the pain with a line of length equal to its magnitude or longer; and pause your hand for a moment and strengthen that until you incise the artery and bring about inflammation up to the bone."
"However, it is necessary that you guard against the continuity of the mandible, which is moved by mastication; and that the nerve is not burned nor the nerves that move it; and that spasms do not occur."
"And if it is about the caution and care of blood flow from the artery that is opened, because in the opening of it there is fear, especially for those who do not know what they are doing and are not studied nor practiced; leave the operation at the beginning."
"And I come with remembrance of the regulation of accidental blood flow from the artery according to its manner, in its place in this book."
"And if you see this illness that does not abate with this cautery and you see the patient's condition tolerable, then cauterize it in the middle of the head as we have recounted before, and cure the ulcer until it is healed."
"And if you wish, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the stricture of artery with cautery having two catheters, and this is better cautery and more confirmative."
"Chapter Five."
"On the Cauterization of Earaches."
"When in the ear there is pain due to friction and it is cured with laxative causes and other cures that have been mentioned in the division, but the pain is not removed, then heat the cautery, which is called puncta, of which this is its shape:"
"And when it has been heated, apply it around the entire ear as if a wheel is turned, or in the circuit of each one if the pain is in each one." "And go along with the cautery to the root of the ear little by little until you feel the spot with your tent."
"And if you cauterize with ten punctures around the entire ear, and it is sufficient, then cure those spots until they are healed."
"Chapter Six."
"On Cauterization of Dizziness."
"Dizziness that is cured with cautery is only of those species which come from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of illnesses."
"Avoid cauterization for the species that occurs due to dryness or spasms of nerves."
"When treating that type of tumor with herbs and caper spurge and garlic, if your treatment does not help, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, the second a little below their temple, and the third at the junction of two lips."
"Then pause your cautery in the contrary direction to where the wound is, for softening only occurs on the part that appears sound."
"And the manner of cauterization is such that you cauterize it with the cautery on the right side of the tip of the ear, then slightly above the horn of the head, and on the temple, whose length should be equal to the length of your finger, and pause your hand with the cautery until it has consumed about half the thickness of a rope."
"And this is the form of the cautery, which is specific to barbers, and its shape is described before us." "But it is still more subtle than what you see here; and it would be better to cut away excess roughness in place of unnecessary delicacy."
"And apply the cure with that which is described in its proper place until it is healed."
"Chapter VII."
"On cauterizing ancient stroke (apoplexy)."
When apoplexy is ancient and the cure for it is what we have said, and the patient does not confirm your medicine but has no fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries: on all the horns of his head; and one cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said; and another cautery on the cheek. And the manner of cauterizing is done according to what has been said above.
Now cauterize over the mouth of the stomach, and it should be more recent; then it shall be cured with what you will prescribe.
Chapter VIII
On cauterizing for oblivion caused by a tumor.
"Give the patient at the beginning large jars and purifying pills."
"And then cover the entire head of the sick person, pausing on its crown, place the plaster described in the treatise on plasters."
"And pause for some time, because this is a manner of cautery." "And do this according to that methodical order which I have already mentioned."
"If this does not heal well, then perform three cauteries on the last part of his head, which should be descending from the most superior part of the head toward the most inferior part of the neck." "And pause between each cautery for the thickness of a finger, and then immediately dress the cautery with what has been produced."
"But if you see that the patient tolerates this badly, then perform the cautery in the middle of the head; but if you want greater cautery, then cauterize him on both temples."
"And dress it immediately until it is healed; and let the cauteries be round according to the shape mentioned before."
"Chapter IX."
"Burning of parasites and softening of the entire body."
"After preparing the head with erasures and water as we have said; then remove the patient's hat, and burn that area with a cautery in the middle of the head, and apply cauteries to all the corners of the head, and apply cauteries to the back part of it, and apply three cauteries to the cervical vertebrae."
"And if it is necessary to soften the body too much in illnesses that are poorly tolerated and the illness is severe, then apply four cauteries on the lumbar vertebrae, and also apply a cautery on the sacrum between the buttocks, lifting up the thigh." "And also cure that area with olive oil, after it has healed, using a cautery."
Chapter .x.
"On cauterization for epilepsy."
"No one is cauterized except in the case of epilepsy caused by phlegm."
"And therefore at the beginning of the illness, prepare the brain with erasures and the other treatment which we have said in the division when the illness is great and poorly tolerated except for medications."
"And if the child cannot tolerate medications, then administer gargarisms and mastigators to soften the brain, for several days before, with beneficial diet."
"And also shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head according to the manner previously mentioned, and another cautery on the occiput of it, and cauterize each corner of the head." "And let it be cauterized with olive oil according to what has been said previously."
"But if the illness is in a child, then pause and use subtle cauteries in this manner:"
Chapter .xi.
"On cauterization for melancholy."
"When the causes of melancholy are corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with cauteries as mentioned earlier, having paralysis."
"And if the cause of melancholy is declining towards it due to excess, and the body of the patient is humid, then let him drink that which cleanses the brain according to what has been mentioned earlier in this division."
"And also shave the head of the patient, and then make a small poultice well-made of it on the circle, and then place it in the middle of the head."
"And let the patient be seated comfortably, and let him be held by someone from every part."
"And also apply a liniment, and then it is worthy of being rubbed with lamb's fat." "And heat it on the fire for gentle warmth by measure, which the patient should suffer when it is applied to him." "And then place it in the middle of the head of the patient within the circle, and leave it until it has cooled down."
"And do this with the patient once a week until he is healed, with the other regimen of him being well; or if you wish, cauterize it making small punctures according to his strength, but keep your hand with such an arranged cautery: this is a special cautery which moistens the brain with equality."
"And then apply that poultice wrapped in a bandage or a piece of wool."
Chapter .xii
"On cauterization for descending water in the eye."
"When it has been declared to you that the beginning of water in the eye has appeared through the signs which I have mentioned earlier in this division, then begin and give the patient to drink what cleanses his head, and protect him from all humidity."
"And make him take a bath with hot water for several days."
"And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head; and also cauterize it with two cauteries on both temples if it is the beginning of descent of water in both eyes, or on one temple if it is the beginning of water in one eye."
"Incise with a cautery all the veins and arteries which are close to the neck; and let the cauteries be in that length on the level of the temples."
"And guard yourself from fluxes of blood when it is cauterized; and if you see any fluxes of blood, stop them with some medicine, which is at your disposal."
"And I will come with wisdom in the extraction of arteries and in the ablation of those and caution concerning fluxes of blood."
"And sometimes it is cauterized on the back of the neck near two bones with two cauteries producing smoke."
Chapter .xiii

"When tears of the eyes are old and abundant, and it is found that this is due to thick phlegmatic excess in the veins and arteries which are manifested on the surface of the head, then cauterize it with a cautery as mentioned in the chapter on the beginning of water rising in the eyes, and with a cautery in the middle of the head and with two cauteries on the back of the neck near the temples, and with two cauteries on the back of the neck near two bones." "Chapter XV."
"Regarding cauterization for drooping eyelids."

"Chapter XVI"
"Regarding cauterization of the eyelid when the hairs are turned inward and piercing the eye:"
"When the hairs of the eyelid are turned inward so as to pierce the eye, cauterize them either with fire or with medicine that burns."
"If you cauterize with fire, first tell the patient to pull out his hairs like those who pluck them for depilation, until they are elongated and hardened; and if it pierces there, then stretch the eyelids with a bandage so that it is not harmed while the hairs are growing."
"Therefore, when they are grown and hardened, then have the patient hold his head steady in the air, and press the eyelid of the eye with a probe, shaped like a mortar leaf, and let the beginning of the probe be close to the hairs."
"And then pause on that spot by immersing it in powdered alum or mucilage of pimpernel on the eye."
"And then ignite the cautery, whose shape is like this:"
"And then cauterize along the figure which is marked here, bit by bit, with several glances, until its surface burns completely, just like a myrtle leaf."
"The sign of the good deed is that you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and its hairs raised above the puncture of the eye."
"Then raise your hand and leave him for three days, and then pause on that spot with a bandage until the scar is healed." "And then treat it with ointment until it heals."
"But if the hairs return again for some cause and the eyelid becomes softened, then do the cautery once more on that spot just as you had done initially."
"But if the hairs are still on the eyelid, then cauterize them until they are raised to their natural place and hardened, so that they do not pierce the eye."
"But if you use a cautery with burning medicine, then order the patient to pull out his hairs until they are elongated and hardened, and then make a paper from cloth in the shape of a myrtle leaf."
"And then take known soap and live coal ashes an ounce each, or whatever you have, and then mix those ashes well, and do this with haste so that it does not get cold; and then spread this on the paper made like a myrtle leaf shape, and place this over one eye or both eyes; and place some of that on the spot of the eye immersed in powdered alum, and let the patient's head be held upright."
"And then place your finger on the medicine and press it gently without harming him until the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for biting is like that of fire."
"And then when he perceives that it feels like biting, then remove the medicine and wipe it with your finger; and then when the biting stops, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water; and then consider if sometimes the eyelid is already raised just like it was washed from constriction with fire or incision, for then it is good; and if not, then return to that medicine on the spot where it has not been applied before and do not relent until your operation is hardened and the eye is contracted."
"And then place a bandage on that spot until the scar of adhesion is healed, and then treat it with ointment or some other thing until it heals."
"And it is necessary that you, during your operation, guard with vigilant diligence that no dirt from the medicine falls into the eye, and if the eyelid becomes softened after several days and some hairs again pierce the eye for some cause, then repeat your medication on that spot where the eyelid has become softened, and exactly as you did at the beginning, and then heal it."
"And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf:"
"And know that human eyes are diverse according to their magnitude and smallness, and therefore your contraction should be made accordingly."
"And do not close the path of rectitude towards anyone who studies in this art."
"Chapter XVII."
"On the cautery of a fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye."
When you treat a fistula as we have mentioned in the divisions of illnesses and your treatment is ineffective, then you should cauterize it in this manner: command the patient to place their head on their own seat, and hold their head steady with some assistant's hands so that it is neither moved nor agitated by their head.
And then pause a piece of gauze or cotton wool soaked in hot wax or pitch on the wound, covering it completely.
And now ignite the cautery which is in this form:
which is cone-shaped, like the shape of a reed or vulture's feather, at one extremity where the cautery is made
And if you wish, it may be penetrating into the other extremity. And if you want, it can come out like this:
But that which is cone-shaped is better for your work.
"Then press on the abscess if it is open, and draw out its liquid and dry it." "And if it's not open, then lance that area and extract the pus from it."
"And then apply the cauterizer that has been well ignited, and press it on that area with a little force at the beginning of the nose, so that you do not burn your hand or disturb the patient, and then pause the cauterizer in the wrinkles of the skin and char it."
"If at the beginning of your cauterization it enters into the bone, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization once or twice if necessary; and leave that area thus for three days, and then apply to that wound with a border and surroundings with a drying ointment until it heals."
"But if eleven days have passed and it is not healed, then apply to it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and scrape it according to what is suitable in its chapter."
"And another method of cauterizing a fistula is that which was first described as follows: enter into the location of the fistula and burn it with this thin camphor wax of the shape of the fistula. Cauterization of a fistula in the mouth
When an apostema forms on the uvula or palate or tonsils and it bursts and becomes infected, and then breaks open and a fistula is formed, you should clean it out and not neglect its treatment. Of cauterization of teeth and softening of gum abscesses.

Then quickly withdraw your hand, and repeat the cauterization several times according to what you desire.
Then have the patient rinse their mouth with saltwater and hold it there for an hour, then spit it out. For the affected tooth will be solidified, the softened gum strengthened, and the corrupted moisture dried up.

"If the matter is not removed from it, then you know that it is penetrating or that the bone is corrupted nearby, or that this is due to one of those causes which will be mentioned later in its place."

"Chapter XLVI."
"On cauterization for torsion."
"When pain occurs in some members due to overexertion or blow and persists for a long time without being relieved by treatment with medicines, then cauterize with a pointed cautery."

"Chapter XLVII."
"On cauterization for leprosy."
"Some lepers are viewed with caution due to great harm and little improvement, especially those whose condition is caused by decay of phlegm and melancholy."
"Therefore, when you wish to cauterize this one, consider if the leprosy is common or already cured according to what we have said in the division above. Do not give it, if there isn't any, and fear that the corruption might spread throughout their whole body and entire complexion. Therefore, cauterize this one on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, another towards the end of the hairline, and two on both horns; and one behind, on the nape or servants."

"And if the leprosy has already spread over the malady and appears manifestly, then you should cauterize this one with those cauteries which we have mentioned for the head; and cauterize on the extremity of the nose with two cauteries on each cheekbone, two on both shoulder blades, six on the spinal processes of the back, and one large on the spinal process near the coccyx, one on the coccyx itself, two on each ankle, one on each heel, two on each toe, two on the knees, and two on the muscles. Cauterize this one over all the joints of these members and feet, and on each sole of their feet, and on the cushions of their soles."
"And beware that you do not cauterize those nerves which are situated on the sole that you may not burn them."

"And know that the more closely you apply cauteries, the greater is the benefit and advantage. And know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as they do with their own sores, because the body of the sufferer is already anesthetized."

Chapter XLVIII

"Chapter XLIX"

**Chapter 53.**
**On Cautery for Wounds and Similar Conditions.**
Often seen in the parts left by the sick foot that is called claw, and it is a thick, solid cause which presses on the foot; and cautery in these cases follows two manners: namely cautery with fire and cautery with cold water.
Cautery with fire is done using a cautery device similar to the shape of a vulture's feather quill, which should be made of iron according to the size that contains the claw on each side, and it should have fine edges.
Then pause the heat of the cautery device on the claw and then slowly move your hand with the cautery device around the circumference of the claw until it reaches the depth of the claw. Leave that for three days until it begins to scar over Then apply a poultice made of crushed wild mallows mixed with salt on that area and leave the poultice overnight, because it will draw out its roots.
Then treat the location with an ointment made from fatty tissue until it is healed.
And if it does not improve, and often happens on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet, then you should administer cautery with cold water in those cases. Take a canula made of bronze or iron or vulture feather, and place it on the claw; then pour a little cold water into the canula, and hold your hand still, pressing the edge of the canula onto the root of the claw while allowing the cold water to flow through the opening at the front of the root of the claw. Wait for a moment until you feel the bite of the cold water for about an hour, then remove it, because the claw with its roots will be eradicated.
Do likewise to the others until all of them are eradicated from your body.
Then cleanse those pustules where the roots of the claws have been eradicated with an ointment that causes the flesh to grow.
Chapter LIV
On cautery for trembling.
When someone has trembling due to inflammation of the nerves or fever caused by heat, or for another similar reason, then you should perform cautery on them with four cauteries or five, placed on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with one cautery; and also place a cautery on the sole of their foot and on their stomach, using an olive-sized cautery.
And may his trembling cease, and may his health be restored quickly from the burning illness.
Chapter LV
On cautery for accidental wounds of the body
When the body is wounded with accidental wounds, and there are pustules or cracks that have been formed from corrupted and thick matter, then at the beginning of the appearance it should be cauterized on top of the fistula head with a subtle cautery made from myrtle wood, the extremity of which has been burned in fire; or with long roots of resinous herbs; or with a lenticular cautery.
And thereafter, as often as it appears, it should be cauterized in the same manner at the beginning of its expulsion; and they should not be believed to be healed until the excess has been disrupted and expelled from them.
But nonetheless, it is necessary that this be done after evacuation with phlebotomy.

"Chapter VII."
"Of the treatment of obstruction of ears."
Some children sometimes exit from the bellies of their mothers unperforated, and this has happened to some men, opacity in the meat of the ear for plague or for flesh born there; and this opacity sometimes is made in the front of the tube of the ear which does not conceal the appearance, and sometimes it is in the parts outside.

Chapter XVI
On Incision of Nail and Removal of Carnal Protrusion from Lacrimal Ducts
You should know that there are two kinds of nails: one is nerve-like, similar to hard, fine matter; the other is not nerve-like and resembles congealed white humor. When you cut this latter type with a knife, it can be easily gripped with tweezers and then removed without the tweezers getting stuck inside.
Both kinds of nails begin only in the larger lacrimal ducts and gradually increase, covering the eye and preventing light and movement of the eye.
To operate for the incision of this nail, the patient should hold their head still and look up. Then open the eye widely with your fingers and lift the eyelid with your hand. Using tweezers with little duplication, grasp the nail and gently pull it upwards at its ends. Then take a needle and thread through it a horsehair or cowhair or oxhair or similar strong hair. Fold the tip of the needle and insert it into the middle of the nail. Then pass the needle through the nail and grasp it with forceps. Gently pull the nail upwards at its ends, and carefully remove the lateral edge of the nail that covers the pupil using the thread. And so you continue removing it until the end is reached.
Then incise the remaining nail at its root using fine scissors or small forceps. This will release the natural lacrimal tissue and prevent continuous tearing from occurring due to the incision.

If the nail is not nerve-like and you cannot insert the needle or grasp it with tweezers, then sometimes this type of nail can be treated with medications. In such cases, follow the methods described in the division (treatment) section.
If you wish to incise the nail, first open the patient's eye and take a fine spoon-shaped knife made of sharp steel with a point like this: Sharp and subtle. Then close the eye for another day.

Then continue your operation on that nail until it is healed.

Chapter XXIV
On the treatment of flesh torn in the nose.
When in the nose there are diverse pieces of flesh attached from which one cause is that it is assembled like a scorpion with many feet, or like a polyp with weight; and this illness is called "polyp" because it resembles that fish represented. And its flesh is cancerous, pale, of dark color; but the lion's flesh is not of dark color.
Therefore in that which is in these lion-like but not fraudulent or cancerous flesh, you should squeeze the illness between your hands and put it in the sun, and draw out its moisture and cut off those pieces of flesh. And then extract that from the openings of its exterior, and then cut what you have comprehended of those with a sharp subtle spatula on one side until you know that all the flesh is removed; but if there remains any cause for which amputation is possible, then remove it with one of the subtle instruments easily so that nothing remains. But if there is bleeding or an abscess forms, then pause until it stops naturally; but if they are malignant abscesses, then cut and cauterize that until the bleeding stops and all cavities are opened.
And then sprinkle it in the nose with wine vinegar and water or wine. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds moisture into the palate, then you know that it is healed.
But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you know that there is still flesh torn on the projecting bones of the nostrils which have not received amputation.
Therefore you should then insert lead into it which has some thickness, and push it in the most of its nostrils, and pause between each push for the amount of one finger or more, and generate the illness and insert an extremity of the lead into the nose with wax or with another cause that is possible.
And after that has been done, let them throw their head backwards so that the odor reaches the canals of the nostrils, and let it be poured over their throat, for several times children at school do this action and it is an easy cause for anyone who wants to do it.
And then pause the two extremities of the lead, one extremity that exits over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a suture of flesh on the holes that are in the lead, and do this until you know that the flesh is with the holes of the lead.
And then extract the lead, and pause in the nose with the abstraction of blood once a day, and do this for three days or more until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh.
And then at the end of the cause, pause in the nose a cannula of lead for seven days until it is healed.
If you intend to treat by cauterization, use the cautery.
This is the form of the purge-making instrument with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nostrils:
And make this of silver or copper, resembling a small open lantern, like a small jug, and the mouth likewise.
And if you wish, make it a closed cannula like a reed, and the cannula of the purge-making instrument should be flat and open; have a handle on its end with which to hold it when pouring in the oil or water that you want from the saps and succulent causes.
Chapter XXV
**Of the thills or wicks that are placed at the extremities of the nose.**
Many times it happens that the eye appears in the extremities of the nose, and is enlarged and swollen during those days when much attention is paid to its care.
And for this reason you should insert it at the beginning of the appearance of that, and erase everything after that. Moreover, pause over the place where cauterization or medicine burns is situated instead of it.
But if its insertion is delayed until it has become enlarged, then consider whether it is hard, thick, dark in color, and insensitive. If this is the case, do not touch that with iron because it may be a malignant carbuncle. Many times that which you have inserted into this carbuncle becomes stuck there due to great mischief on that person.
And if the carbuncle is of a reddish color and not dark in color, sometimes insertion may be possible everywhere. In this case, evacuate the morbid matter and insert without fear, and cure the place with something that dries and constricts until it is healed.
Chapter XXVI
Of the suture of the nose, lips, and ear when continuity has been dissolved by an ulcer or wound.
Know that when there is a dissolution of continuity in one of these cartilages (the nose, lips, or ear), little confidence should be placed in that operation, except with certain skilled individuals.
Therefore, when you encounter such a cause in someone, first examine whether it is a fresh wound with its own blood. Then immediately approximate the two lips of the wound with suture and apply proper dressing until healed.
And if the lips of the continuity have already separated and each is free from infection, then it is necessary to cut off each end of its apparent cord until there is no bleeding. And then closely approximate the two lips with suture and press them together. Then sprinkle dragon's blood powder on it and apply a poultice of diaphoretic plaster or another consolidative plaster, leaving that dressing for two or three days before removing it and replacing it. Leave it until the wound has healed by itself.
But the manner of suture is to join the edges of the continuity either with needles as recommended for abdominal closure, or else with thread in such a way that you know how to do it.
Chapter XXVII
Of the extraction of those causes that come between the two lips within wounds
Many times it happens that in the midst of the lips of wounds there are hard pimples resembling pig fat, some small and others larger.
"Therefore you should examine each of those hardnesses and divisions, and then make an incision in the place where the blood is concentrated, wash it with vinegar, and dress the wound with something that has astringent properties until it heals."
Capítulo XXVIII.
Chapter XXVIII: On the Incision of Adherent Tissue in the Gums
Often there appears on the gum adherent flesh which the ancients called albulus; therefore you should suspend it with forceps or hold it with your fingers and cut it off at its root, allowing the sound tissue to bleed freely.
And afterwards apply to the place where it has been cut a powder that is both astringent and cicatrizing.
And if that flesh returns, cut it again afterwards, and cauterize it so that it does not return again.
Capítulo XXIX.
"Due to teeth made of iron."
When the surface of the teeth in both jaws and those in front are tightly sealed with rough, sharp, thick deposits, sometimes blackened, and have green or yellow pus between them and the gum, this indicates decay and the teeth are loose.
Therefore you should seize the patient between your hands and place their head on the pillow of their bed, hold open their mouth in which those deposits appear and cause such sand-like grit to arise from them that there is no cause for any decay, and this is done with respect to blackness and yellowness and other things that are altered.
Therefore if this is what you want in the beginning of the reason, well then; but otherwise, later you should repeat the reason on those days two and three until it comes to its final statement in what you wish.
And know that teeth require various types of tools with different shapes and forms according to the preparation for your operation. And therefore choose the rasp with which you remove the tooth from within the teeth that is different from the rasp with which you scrape between the teeth in other ways. These forms of rasps should be prepared by you, as you will soon see:
Capital thirty
Extraction of teeth
But when you care for a tooth with all your skill and patience in its extraction, there is no reason why the vision should not be clear once it has been extracted, because it is a substance that becomes sublime during the extraction.
But if the patient is forced to have a tooth extracted, you must be absolutely certain which is the painful tooth, for often the pain seems to come from a healthy tooth, and you extract one while the pain continues until the truly diseased and painful tooth is removed, as we have seen happen in barbers' operations.
Therefore, when you are certain which is the painful tooth and know it well, then you should scarify around the tooth with spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the gum completely severed, and immediately remove that with your tweezers, or with subtle forceps bit by bit until it comes out.
And then with strong forceps hold the tooth firmly for good traction or extraction, and pause the head of the patient between your thumbs so that you may have it well held that it does not move, and extract the tooth directly in such a manner that you do not break it, nor cause greater pain to the patient.
And then if it is not forgotten, take one of those instruments and put it behind the tooth on all sides with ease and effort to loosen it as was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is cracked or decayed, then you must fill that crack and strengthen it with the extremity of a fine wire before tightening it with forceps on that tooth.
And you must work carefully with scarification around all sides of the gum and guard your strength so that you do not break it or cause it to shatter apart from it, and return on the patient for greater good than the first pain of him.
And beware that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their haste and audacity to eradicate teeth without administering what we have recommended; for many times they cause great illnesses upon men which are more difficult to treat than the tooth itself, and leave behind roots of removed teeth all together, or some of those, or extract it with some bones of the jaw as is often testified.
And when extracting it, wash the mouth with hot water or vinegar with salt.
And if there are flows of blood from that, as often happens, then take some quantity of sage and sprinkle it on the wound, and if it does not suffice that sage, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and fine tweezers with which the tooth is held at the beginning should be of long extremity, short handle, and thick, so that they are not bent when using them.
And let them be thus shaped with grooves on the inside of the thick handle such that when you tighten with those, they are not bent, and have short extremities.
And let them be made of wrought iron, straight-edged, and on the extremities have teeth that interlock with each other for strong tightening, and sometimes the extremities are shaped like the beak of a bird called ciconia, which is wide, and they are of great force.

Chapter 32
Of the care of prominent teeth above the others.

However, if it is not attached to another tooth, then cut that one with this instrument, whose shape resembles a pig's snout, made of sharp-edged Indian iron."

"And if it is a tooth with a broken edge that irritates the tongue, then you should grind down that rough portion until it is smooth and flattened, so that the tongue is not injured and speech is not impeded."
"Chapter XXXIII"
"Of restoring broken teeth with gold or silver foil."
"When teeth are broken by concussion or removal due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot chew their food, and you have treated it with astringent medicines, but your treatment has not been effective, then it is proper to restore those that are strong with gold foil, not silver, because silver turns green over time, but gold never changes."
"And the foil should be made thin and fine according to the amount that can fit between the teeth. The method of preparation is as follows: take the foil and fold it twice between two healthy teeth, then carefully twist the folds of the foil between one or more broken teeth so that it reaches the healthy part of the other tooth." "And then continue the filling within the portion where you began, and carefully press your hand with ease and skill so that it is not broken."
"And make sure to press the foil tightly against the roots of the teeth so that it does not become loose."
"And then cut off the excess ends of the foil with forceps or scissors, gather them up at each location, and bend them down and hide them between the healthy tooth and the broken tooth, so that they do not injure the tongue." "And then press it tightly as with wax."
"But if it becomes loose or broken, then repair it or them with other foil in this same manner at all times."
"And this is the form of teeth and the figure of the restoration of two healthy teeth and two broken ones, as shown in this drawing:"
"And when one or two teeth return to their proper place after falling out due to concussion and have been restored as we have described, but still become broken again."
"And this is only done by skilled and knowledgeable artists."
"Sometimes it is appropriate to use bones from cattle. They are shaped like teeth and placed in the location where the tooth has failed. It is then bound tightly as we have said, and remains there serving for a long time."

Chapter XXXIV
"This ligament which sometimes prevents the tongue from moving or is naturally present but accidentally occurs due to phlegm that has already congealed."

"Chapter XXXV."
"For removal of a ranula from under the tongue."
Sometimes, a small tumor resembling a pea grows under the tongue and hinders its natural movement.
The operation involves opening the patient's mouth widely towards the sun and examining the tumor.
And if you find it to be dark colored or black, hard, and the patient feels no pain, then do not touch that which is cancerous.
And if it is inclined towards whiteness, indicating humidity, then you should use a spoon to remove it, and carefully cut that thin sputum with scissors, cutting it entirely; but if blood comes during your operation, then pause for a moment until the bleeding stops, applying some powdered vitriol to restrict its flow.
And then return to your work until you have removed it completely with care, rinsing the wound with vinegar and salt; and heal it with another cure until it is healed.
Capítulo XXXVI
Chapter XXXVI: Extraction of Tumors from the Ears and Those Found in the Throat, as Well as Other Tumors.
When there are tumors in the throat that are swollen glands which sometimes become enlarged and protrude externally, these are called "ears," and when you treat them with water as mentioned earlier but they do not heal, then consider whether the tumor is hard, dark colored, and causes little pain. If so, do not touch it with iron.
"It is of red color and has a large root, therefore do not touch it with iron due to blood flow. Rather, let it remain until it ripens, then you shall remove it or break it apart yourself."
"If it is white in color and has a fine root, then that one should be incised."
"And before your operation, consider the condition of the abscess: whether it has already ripened and is fully ready, or if it has decreased in size with some diminution. Then make the patient lie down facing the sun, with their head towards the east, open their mouth wide, and the servant holding their tongue with a suitable instrument, whose form is as follows:"
"And it should be made of silver or brass, and be sharp like a knife."
"Then, while pressing the tongue with that instrument and exposing the abscess to you, take courage and cut into it at once, inserting the knife gently into the opening and pulling outwards as much as possible." "After that, if some of the tunics come out along with it, then immediately cut them off with this instrument, whose form is as follows:"
"After that, if some of the tunics come out along with it, then immediately cut them off with this instrument, whose form is as follows:" "And it resembles forceps, but its ends are curved such that the tips of each face inward towards the other, being very sharp, and made of iron with a brass inlay."
"But if this instrument is not available to you, then cut it with a scalpel whose form is as follows: It should be sharp on one side and not sharp on the other."
"And after making one cut, make another according to this same method of incision. Then wash the wound clean with water."
"But if there is bleeding from the wound, wash it clean with water from a decoction of rosehip or myrtle leaves, adding to that any of the astringent causes at hand until the bleeding stops. Then dress the wound until it heals."
"And sometimes you may find other abscesses near those two ears, and cut them according to what I have said regarding the incision of two equal cuts."
"And now I will tell you about a woman who was afflicted with an abscess that had formed in her groin. It was dark colored and insensitive, the wound had already closed up, she was breathing with difficulty, and eating and drinking water were prohibited to her. She would have died within two days or less if something hadn't been done."
"And the abscess had grown so large that it had produced two branches that extended out through two tracks."
"I then carefully inserted my hand into one of their orifices and pulled out that which was stuck there, and indeed a large portion of it was drawn out. Then I pushed in the other end that I could comprehend of the other passage, and then I opened its mouth and compressed its tongue. Then I left the orifice in that abscess."
"And indeed a large part of it was cut off from him, and only a little blood flowed from him." "Then the swelling of that woman subsided, and she immediately began to drink water, and indeed she took food. Therefore I did not cease to insert into that abscess many times over a long period of time, and it succeeded in healing the abscess in place of that which was prolonged."
"So I then took a cautery and burned the swelling of it, so that it might be completely removed. Then I wandered around and did not know what God had done with that one."
"Chapter XXXVII."
"On the Incision of a Swelling When It Is Abscessed."
"When catarrh descends to the swelling and it is abscessed and prolonged, then it is called perpendicular. And if it is located on the side of a fat person and is round, then it is called bubo."
"But when it is healed with that which we have said in the division, and does not confirm your cure, and indeed many times an abscess that has been cauterized is already completely healed and is thin, then it is necessary to insert into that which is aggregated roundly. And if it is at that length, and is sanguineous, of dark color or black, and does not have a center, then it is necessary to beware of the incision of it, for in that there is fear concerning illness."
"And when you see it according to the manner which I have described concerning its whiteness and length, that you make the illness cease and press the point of it with an instrument whose shape is processed thus and immediately place the onci in the new one and pull that downwards and incise it with one of those instruments which are mentioned in the incision of two melons."
"And it is necessary not to incise that except what is adapted over the natural term without addition, for if you incise more of it, you will cause its death."
"And immediately after the incision, use that which we have recommended in the incision of two melons, and heal it so that it may be healed."
"But if the illness is frightened by the incision of it, then it is necessary to use a poultice in its cauterization without fear, and the manner of cautery on it is not except with hot water, and it is that you press the head of the swelling on its surface, and immediately press the point of it with the instrument which we have mentioned, and immediately take some of that hot water which we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and pour it with that live cause, and pause it neither thick nor thin, and from there you fill the cavity of the instrument whose shape is this:
"Place the end of it in the cavity where the medicine is applied like the cavity of a spoon's handle. Place the instrument with the medicine on the vulva and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva or mucus from their mouth does not flow down through the inserted medicine into their throat, causing harm."
"Then press on the medicine with your mouth for about half an hour until you see that it has darkened and moistened from the warmth of your mouth."
"If you wish, take cotton and wrap it around the end of the ray. Submerge the cotton in the medicine, then insert the ray with the cotton into a cannula until the cotton adheres to that cannula. Repeat this process as many times as needed until you achieve the desired cauterization of the wound, and leave it alone for three or four days until it dries up."
"And if you need to repeat the application of the medicine, do so. And after cauterization, clean the wound's perimeter with cotton soaked in boric acid, and rinse it with water that has been boiled. Then dress it with ointment and bandage it properly until it heals."
"And this type of treatment was saved from incision and prolonged fear."
"Sometimes the uvula is cured with such subtlety that it does not require cauterization or incision, as it can be treated by sublimation in this manner: take calamint, hyssop, origanum, rue, saffron, camomile, brayd and similar herbs. Adjust all these ingredients, or some of them, in a mortar, and soak them with sour wine, then boil them. Let the mortar be well covered with decent lut, and in the middle of the mortar place a tube on which to set an enameled silver or brass instrument shaped like this:
The extremity has been inserted into the mouth of the patient while the vapour rises to the uvula causing it to become obscured.
Proceed to rub that moist cloth until it becomes dry, and make sure not to perform this cure at the beginning of the appearance of abscesses, as it would be too tight on the abscess. Instead, you should declare the abscess of the cautery.
But if this instrument is not present, then take a reed and attach a cloth to its end, so that the mouth of the patient may be covered. For the cloth will prevent vapour from burning the mouth.
This cure is good for health.
Chapter 38
Of the extraction of thorns and that which adheres in the throat, and other causes.
"Often adhesions form on the bladder or spine of the foot due to some other cause."
"Then you must remove what is visible of that [tumor], on which the sight falls, because when you press the tongue with an instrument beforehand, it will be declared to you what is in the throat."

Or the patient can swallow a piece of bread or some lettuce or a sip of water; or take a piece of dry sea sponge and tie it tightly with thread, and then make the patient swallow it, because when it reaches the spot where its spines are stuck, they will be removed at that time." "Chapter XXXIX."
"Of removing a bloodsucker attached to the throat."
"When a bloodsucker has been treated with what we have said in the division of cure with medications and does not improve, then consider the throat of the patient under sunlight, because you should have prepared the tongue of it with that instrument which we have described."
"Then if you see the bloodsucker, remove it carefully with tweezers or gently with your fingers."
"And if it is not possible for you to remove it with that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the patient's throat, and in the concavity of the cannula place a hot iron, and do this many times (until the bloodsucker is dead and removed from the throat) and make sure that the patient abstains from water all day."
"And then take a vein full of water that has been heated, and open the mouth of the patient into it, and wash his mouth with it; and do not let any cause remain in that water and hold it for an hour more with your hand, because the bloodsucker immediately feels the water cold."
"But if it is not removed with what we have described, then fumigate the patient with incense or asafoetida through that instrument which we have described in the fumigation of the uvula."
"Do this, until he falls asleep."
"And there is another way of operating in the fumigation of that, which is to take an earthenware vessel in which there are hot coals and cover it with a cloth, with a hole in the middle of it through which the extremity of the instrument should be placed; and then begin the fumigation; and place the patient's mouth on the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not escape until you know that the fumigation has reached the bloodsucker, because the bloodsucker will immediately fall asleep."
"And if it does not fall asleep, then repeat the fumigation many times, and make sure that the patient abstains from drinking and eating salty foods and salt, and does not drink water, because this regimen is necessary for him to follow."
"And this is the shape of the instrument with which bloodsuckers are removed from the throat when they are seen; it resembles tweezers like these, except that it has some curvature:" "The one placed on the guolayro, its extremity being like the beak of a stork, that is a glove in which the sharpness of a file has been inserted."
"Chapter XL."
"This one is about the sum of the discourse on the opening of apostemes and their sectioning."
"Different kinds of apostemes, with many different characteristics according to their memory, each one discussed in this book."
"And they are diverse in their perforation and sectioning for two different methods: one of which is specific to embedded apostemes; and what we learn about humidity."
"And the second method is for those locations where accidents occur in the body, because the aposteme that occurs on the head differs from one that occurs on the buttocks; and likewise, an aposteme that occurs in a fleshy location differs from one that occurs at a joint; and each has its own treatment through operation."
"More about apostemes: some of which should not be perforated but await maturity or completion of their healing."
"There are other apostemes which should be removed when they become hardened, even if they have not reached maturity according to their completion: like those that are close to joints. For an aposteme near a joint, its evil extends into the surrounding area and often corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing contraction of that limb; or it is near a main member, and if you delay perforation until it is ripe, the main member may suffer harm; or it is near the buttocks, therefore perforate it before it becomes hard. And do not perforate one with incomplete digestion, but rather one close to the buttocks, lest its contents enter the rectum and cause elongation into the internal parts of the buttocks, forming a fistula or making healing difficult." "And so you should know the time for perforation of an aposteme, and this is when it has reached maturity."
"And know that an aposteme has reached maturity when there is a cessation of pain and fever, along with a decrease in heat and pulsation, and the tip of the aposteme becomes pointed, along with other signs."
"And know that perforation should be made in the location nearest to the aposteme and where pus has come out from its tip during curettage."
"And always perform perforation along the length of the flesh or body if apostemes are located on the face, buttocks, hands, feet, nerves, arteries; and finally in all locations except those which are reflected, for in these cases use reflection during perforation."
"But when an apostema is in a fleshy location, it is better to leave perforation until digestion has been fully completed, as we have said; for if you perforate it beforehand, the wound of it will extend and much foul matter will be emitted, and often its lips are hardened and its depth increased."
"But some apostemes should be perforated across the width of the flesh or body according to necessity, or according to what that member requires."
"And you should make a small perforation for smaller apostemes, but for larger ones make a large and wide perforation or many sections according to the diversity of their sizes."
"And there are other apostemes in which the chain should be curved and incised when it has become like bread dough and is in a condition where it can already be opened, as happens with those of the groin and buboes."
"And there are those which are incised with three-angle sections, and those in which it is incised like a mitre leaf, as with apostemes on the angles."
"And there are also those in which a round section and a crescent-shaped section are used, similar to those."
"But for that one where it is not like the others, such as superficial lion-like apostemes, you should perforate it with a superficial or flat perforation only."
"And when the aposteme is large and has collected much pus, you should perforate it but do not attempt to remove all the pus at that time; having removed a part of it, then on the following day dress the aposteme again and subsequently remove a larger portion each time until it has healed."
"And even more so if the patient is a young child, or a pregnant woman, or an infant, or an elderly person in decrepitude; for often at the time of pus discharge the animal spirit is resolved and quickly death occurs, and you operate at your peril."
"So heed this chapter with great care, and when performing perforation on these apostemes, be sure to cleanse the wound and consider whether the wound of the aposteme is small or has a flat section; if it is small, then apply a poultice or an ancient cataplasm. But if the apostema is large and its incisions are many, then you must pause between each pull until they come out together."
"And if a part of the chain has become separated or curved in its circuit within the aposteme, then you should close it with silk thread or linen thread, just as when you are tying bread dough or cheese, without moisture; and strengthen it on the third day. Then proceed to treat it with what is appropriate for wounds until it is healed."
"But if blood flow occurs during your operation, then apply a linen cloth dipped in water and vinegar, pressing it against the location of the bleeding several times."
"But if the bleeding persists, then you should apply treatment and care and powders which have been recommended in many places throughout this book and elsewhere."
"But if it is wintertime and the location of the aposteme has many nerves, then you should apply powders made with hot wine and oil, pressing them onto those locations."
"And if it is summertime and the locations are fleshy, then you should apply powders mixed with water and oil or with wine and oil, all of which have been strained until the third day, as we have said. Then dress the aposteme and cleanse it and treat it with whatever is appropriate for its care until it has healed."
"And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of apostemes in general; but according to the way of distinction, I have already spoken specifically about each aposteme and how it should be treated in separate chapters."
Chapter XLII.
"About the incision of apostemes that appear on the chain of the head."
"On the chain of the head there are small apostemes and they have nodes that contain tunics. There are many kinds of them."
"And among them are pimples, some of which contain moisture similar to lime." "And there are those that contain moisture like dust and those that resemble them, and those that are stony and hard."
"And in the sectioning of all these apostemes, there is nothing to fear about their extraction, for they do not cause any harm when extracted."

Of the Incision of Scrofulas that occur on the neck.

Capital XLIV
Regarding the section on aposteme which occurs in the groin area, and is called an inguinal hernia.
This aposteme named hernia of the groin is a large aposteme according to the color of the body, and it is most common in women.
And it occurs in two ways, either naturally or accidentally.
And in the case of the natural one, it cannot be cured.
And the accidental one is of two kinds: the first resembles fat knots, and the other kind resembles an aposteme caused by the obstruction of an artery, in which there is fear. And it is not necessary to make a presumption about this with iron unless it is small. And then you should examine that with your finger and investigate it with the said instrument. And if you find it similar to fat knots, and it is not suspended by any of the veins, then you should cut into it like nodes, and extract it with water containing it from the skin and bursa. And if not, then the whole of its nature should be scrutinized, and the place cured with what is necessary for cure until it is healed.
Capital XLV
Regarding the section on kinds of knots
Of the many kinds of knots, I have already mentioned all their kinds in the division.
And it is necessary for me to point out again the difference between a knot and an exitura (hernia) in case there is any doubt.
Therefore I say that in an hernia there is heat and fever and intense pain until the boiling of the excess moisture is stopped. And it is full putrefaction which then stops the fever, pain, and heat.
But in a knot there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains only chyle or lymph which is proper to the sac itself.
And it appears according to the color of the skin, and its beginning is like a bruise, and it becomes like an empty sac, whether larger or smaller. And there are two kinds: some are fat and contain moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many, as I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a knot, it is necessary for you to examine it and inquire about its beginning with an instrument called intromes, according to what will come next in this chapter.
And this is the manner of inquiry for apostemes and all kinds of knots. You should take this instrument and insert it into the most humid place that you find in the aposteme, and you should move your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the chain.
And then you should lastly withdraw your hand according to the measure of the size of the aposteme, and then withdraw the intromes and consider what is issued in its track.
And if it is forgotten moisture that runs, of whatever color it may be, then you should cut it with a superficial section as I have said in other apostemes.
And if there is no moisture found from the track of the intromes, then you know that it is fat
And cut across it with a cross-section according to this form: Thus as you have taught, suspend that one with a noose, cut the chain from all parts easily, guard the skin or bag if possible over it and extract that corruption at its root.
But if it breaks during the operation, it is not possible to extract that corruption, and many times this happens there, so you should pull it out piece by piece until there remains no cause.
For if there remains any cause, little or much, the knot will return according to its nature.
And if there remains some small part of it, then fill the wound with some corrosive powder and press it down, placing a plaster that draws out the inflammation on top, and cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
And if the knot is large, then cut both lips of it and cure it with what encloses it.
But if there is a pulsating vessel on the contrary, or non-pulsating one, then cut and cauterize the place where it passes that is wet with vitriol, leaving it alone for two days or three until the wound purges itself and its inflammation calms down; and again return to cutting what remains of the knot.

"Chapter on the treatment of prominence of the navel."
"Prominence of the navel is caused by many reasons: either from fissures in the skin above the belly, or from tissue or bowel protruding through other ruptures; or from blood flowing from a vein or artery, as has been said before, or from constricted wind in it."

Chapter 53
On the treatment of cancer.
We have already spoken in the section on cancer of its types and how it can be cured with medicine, and that cure with iron is avoided because it causes ulcers. We have also said that cancer arises from the greatest carelessness in its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer can be eradicated in certain locations, such as those on the breasts or scrotum, and it is especially so when it is caught early while still small.
But when cancer becomes advanced and severe, it is not proper to approach it, because I have never seen any case of such a growth that could be cured by me or anyone else.
And when surgery is necessary for cancer, as we have said, it should be preceded by allowing the disease to run its course and purging with black bile occasionally. Then make an incision if there is a clear sign of fullness or swelling.
Then prepare the patient for surgery by preparing the area where the operation will take place, and then make an incision with a knife that is suitable for the situation. Then excise all affected parts with careful dissection to ensure that no cause of the disease remains. Then allow the blood to flow freely, and do not remove the tissue too lightly. Express the surrounding tissues and wipe away all thick blood with your hand or an appropriate instrument.
But if you have difficulty with thick blood from veins or arteries, then cauterize that area until the bleeding stops. Then dress the wound with appropriate medication until it heals.
