"Chapter 57."
"Of the purification of children and the treatment of what happens to them at circumcision."
Circumcision is not the sole solution for continence as with other plagues. However, when it is our operation and within our will, and this deed is properly performed on children, we should assign to that the best operation and gentle path leading to health.
The ancients did not mention circumcision in all of their books, for they did not use it in their laws. This was because at that time, people had acquired the habit through experience, which is why most craftsmen and barbers practice circumcision using a razor or an awl. They also use liniment with pitch and incise with a fingernail.
"I have already tried all these methods and found no better modification with forceps, linen, or file in circumcision; for many times the skin has slipped away upwards because the foreskin has two tunics, leaving the outer one behind, which often results in another incision and certain pain." Chapter LXIII
Of Incision on Fatty Hernia and Its Treatment
Know that in this section about this hernia, there is fear of losing the patient to danger in the worst dispositions; therefore, it is my view that dismissal of him and saving him by that better means should be considered.
You are also remembering the operation on this one and the specifics of the abscesses.
Therefore, it is said that the abscesses are born in those bodies whose veins are inflamed and this happens for many causes: either by acute severe excess of matter that flows into the veins, or by blows.
And the color of the abscess follows the color of the body, and it is not found in the area of pain, this is a severe abscess.
A hard, lifted abscess has dark coloring, and there is no sensation in it.
And sometimes it happens due to the narrowing of the arteries and by inflammation of those that have already been perceived as remembered from before, or by inflammation of veins.
But what happens due to inflammation of arteries is known by the spreading of the abscess when you compress it with your fingers, and it does not need to be touched.
But that which happens due to inflammation of a vein does not spread from it for any reason, even with compression by the fingers.
And it is possible that on this type of abscess there can be made an incision and on the other flesh; it is to insert the chain of veins, and appropriate stretch out the wound above its parts, and extract that white fluid from it, and release the suspenders of vessels, and tie them up, and incise those suspenders that you have released from all parts of the wound.
Therefore, if the abscess is already united with those flesh parts, then it is necessary to extract that abscess and incise it.
And if there is adhesion within some cause of the fluid or between that which is between the vessels, then it is necessary to release all that adhesion and make a round incision.
But if there is a formation of flesh in the place where the adhesion was which is behind it, then it is necessary to incise all that which is from it and extract the abscess just as we have said.
Therefore, once your operation is complete, then fill the wound with lanolin infused in rosemary oil and wine; and appropriate care for it with another cure until it is healed.

Chapter LXV
"Regarding the treatment of intestinal hernia."

"Then you should insert your finger into that which is the testicle, that is between the white intestine, which lies near the loop of the bowel, and behind it; and then separate it with that adhesion which is in the part behind the loop."
"And then carefully lift the cord of the testicles upwards with your hand, and at the same time extend the white intestine upwards with your left hand, elevating the loop of bowel with the intestine to the part where the incision is made; and then ask the assistant to extend the loop further upwards, and you should dissolve that adhesion which is behind it with a gentle solution."
"And then carefully examine all around that there may be no cause of the bowel being involved in the white tough tunic." "But if you find any cause, then quickly push it back into the abdomen."
"And then make an incision in that part near the cord of the testicles, through which blood and urine may flow freely, as we have advised earlier."
"And then apply lanum soaked in oil to the wound; and then apply the ligature which we have advised (and sometimes cauterize the white tissue near the incision of the blood vessel, as it often happens); and then leave the ligature so that it may fall by itself."
"But if the wound closes slowly, then cold water should be poured on it, and a dressing applied over it so that it may fall away as we have said."
"And then dress the wound with the other treatment for wounds until it is healed."
"Chapter LXVI."
"On Windy Hernia."
"There is no one who has been burned by the treatment of this with iron."
"And the first thing they said was that it should be treated in the same way as the hernia with wine, which is to tie up the vessels near the cut on that side with feacility; and then dry up the middle part around the inflammation with whatever works that; so that the vessels may fall away."
"And dress the wound as we have said until it is healed."
"Chapter LXVII."
"On the Dislocation Which Occurs in Joints."
Some veins sometimes rupture in the ankles as we have said, and it appears enlarged.
And do not give any cause for the intestines to the patient; and if you do give one, it is little; and return in all hours.
But if the time is prolonged with this, an adjusted fissure occurs in the scrotum through which the intestine enters the scrotum; and this happens due to the extension of the scrotum, which is in the ankles as we have said, which causes the scrotum to become extended and softened, and the place becomes inflamed and enlarged.
And its treatment is with cauterization as described above.
And sometimes it is cured with iron according to this manner: and it is that the patient lies on his back between the two thighs, and then dry the place of the rupture of the swollen apostemas by sectioning along its width according to their quantity, three times.
And then strengthen the scrotum white that is below the tailbone so that it may be uncovered.
"Then take the wand and place it on the prominent part of the hip joint, pressing gently on the abdomen."
"And place both prominent locations over the extremity of the hip bone, adjusting one against the other at the suture line."
"And then extract the extremity of the wand, ensuring that you do not touch any part of the hip bone, nor extend it too much, or cause injury as you know how to perform this intestinal hernia cure."
"And then cure it with the treatment for hernias, and if you incise the veins, cleanse them and restore the hernia before it solidifies, because the hip joint contracts and is not adjusted to the prominence of rupture."
"It is better to cauterize at this location, as it is closer to safety."
Chapter LXVII
"Concerning the softening of the spermatic cord."
"Frequently in some men, the chain of the testicles becomes softened because the flesh between them is softened; it is said to be caused by neglect."
"Therefore it is necessary that whoever undertakes the treatment of this patient should make him lie down on his back, and cut all of the softened cord from its natural position; afterwards, he should join the two lips with a suture."
"And if you wish, at the beginning, it is possible to remove the excess of softened cord with three or four stitches and a firm suture."
"Then cut between the sutures; afterwards treat for other diseases until he is healed, and the wounds close."
"The sixty-ninth chapter"
"Of castration."
"Know that castration is condemned in our law, but it is permitted to me to remember this in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except for two ways: the first is because of the science of medicine when one inquires about it, so that he knows how to treat him to whom it happens; the second way is that often we have needed castration of other beasts for our pleasures, such as dogs, goats, pigs, and similar beasts."
"And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by tearing or by cutting with a section."
"In cases caused by contusion, the procedure is to immerse the affected part in hot water until its joints are softened and it is limbered, then hang it." "And then take those with your hand, but only those that are resolved and do not appear to be left behind from the touch."
"In cases of castration done by incision and sectioning, hold the animal firmly and press on the cord of its testicles with your left hand."
"And then tie off the suspension ligament, and make an incision above each cut with a sectioning motion until both testicles have been removed."
"And then cut those that have already separated themselves from the body wall." "Do not leave any cause on those of the scrotum, but rather remove the thin skin which covers the vases."
"And this method of castration is better than that done by contusion because strong contusion leaves no trace of the testicles and causes the animal to desire copulation."
"And then dress the wound until it has healed."
"Chapter LXX."
"Concerning the treatment of hermaphrodism."
"Hermaphrodism in males occurs in two ways: the first is when it appears as a space in the cord of the testicles between which there are two testicles resembling an opening like that of a female, and through which sperm passes."
"And sometimes urine flows from that same cord of the testicles."
"But in females it is one species: that is, the opening of the female above the pelvis is like two testicles of a male, each of which emits a little urine at the time of emission like the penis of a male and two testicles."
"And its treatment is three species: two for males and one species for females." "And it is necessary that you make an incision in those flesh folds where the urine flows out, and then dress them with the same care as other wounds."
"And in the second species of males where urine comes out from the cord of the testicles, there is neither treatment nor operation for it."
"Chapter XXI."
"Concerning lens and prominent flesh caused by females."
"A prominent lens is naturally adjusted during erection and becomes erect due to attention, but sometimes it is enlarged in some females such that it spreads out like in males and enters the vagina during copulation."
"Therefore you should grasp the excess of the lens with your hand or with a hook and make an incision."
"And do not lastly in the incision, especially on the glans penis, lest blood flow."
"And then dress it with the care of wounds until it has healed."
"But flesh born is flesh that appears in the horrific of the mother within which it fills up, and fortunately it is extruded from the openings externally resembling the tail (and thus some first called this “disease of the tail”). Therefore we should incise it just as we do for lens, and dress it until it has healed."
"Chapter LXXII."
"Concerning treatment of arthritis."
"Arthritis is when the opening of the female is not perforated or has a small passage." "And it is either natural or accidental."
"Accidental occurs due to illness that has preceded it, and this is caused by flesh naturally adjusted, or by flesh newly born or thickened skin."
"And it occurs either in the front of the mother or on her sides, or above her pubic bone or below her pubic bone. It prevents coitus and pregnancy and childbirth, and often it prevents menstruation as well."
"And the diagnosis of this is made by examining the opening of the vagina if the obstruction is apparent. But if it is not apparent, you should examine it with your fingers or a probe."
"But if the obstruction is due to thin skin, and it is apparent between the two lips, then you should cut it open."
"And if it stops over the two pubic lips, then carefully insert your fingers on both sides of where it is most thickened."
"And the female should be on her back with her thighs extended. Then carefully pull apart the two lips with force until that thin skin is broken and the obstruction is opened."
"And then take wool moistened in oil and place it on that location. Leave it there for a day so that the skin does not stick together again."
"But if the skin is thick and hard, then you should incise it with a broad spath or with a myrtle leaf."
"But if the obstruction is due to flesh being born, then suspend that flesh with a hook and incise it."
"And apply medicines that stop bleeding without biting, such as achati, dragon's blood, and frankincense mixed with album of egg white."
"And then insert a wide lead cannula to prevent the wound from closing too quickly."
"And keep it like that for several days and apply warm water compresses."
"And then dress it with the usual treatment for consolidation until it has healed."
"And sometimes during birth other flesh is born alongside. If this happens, incise according to the method described above." "But if this is due to an embryonic tumor, then do not cause any injury with iron in any way to that embryonic tumor within the uterus."
"Chapter LXXIII."
"Concerning the treatment of hemorrhoids, prolapse of the rectum, and red tumor that occurs in the opening of females."
"Hemorrhoids are a prominence of many veins around the openings from which blood flows continuously. And when these hemorrhoids become old, they are called piles."
"And I have already spoken in the division about the species and signs of these, and I will say now which ones receive treatment and which do not."
"So I say that hemorrhoids and piles that are in the front of the uterus and cannot be felt do not receive treatment with iron."
"But those which are at the opening of the uterus where you can feel them are those that are treated."
"And you should make the woman lie on her back and then extend her buttocks with forceps or rough cloth and incise those piles with a razor."
"And then sprinkle powder on them that stops bleeding without biting, such as achati or similar ones."
"And then make her lie on her belly for an hour and apply a warm water compress to the wound."
"And if bleeding persists, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and the skins of pomegranates and figs and similar ones."
"And then take barley flour and mix it with honey, vinegar, and wine. Make a poultice with this and apply it on the back of her buttocks."
"And if bleeding is profuse, that is good. But if not, make it adhere with two cupping glasses and apply scarification to the breasts."
"And then take wool and immerse it in juice of coriander or juice of agrimony or juice of garlic with white wine. Make it adhere to the location, and then dress the wound with egg whites until it is healed."
"And dress it until it is healed."
"Chapter LXXIV."
"Of accidental perforation of the bladder in the uterus."
Many species of ulcers occur in the greater part of the body, such as hard and fleshy tumors, and ulcerous growths and inflamed ones, and serpiginous and fistulous ones that are bloody and reddish. And you have already described these illnesses and their species and their symptoms, and their remedies in the division [of the book].
And it is necessary that you should speak in this treatise of cauterizing the ulcer which occurs on the body when it is of those ulcers which are hard to heal, and if you wish to know in what manner the operation is performed with iron.
Therefore it is necessary that you consider whether the pain of the ulcer at its beginning is sharp with percussion and swelling and fever, and if sometimes it reddens and if cats are attracted to it, then do not cut into it with a perforation, but cure it with water which aids in its maturation until the acuteness of the accident ceases.
And then it is necessary that you make the woman lie on her back on two pillows; and let her recline on her shoulders with her heels placed near the edge of the bed outside her belly, and let her legs be extended, and let her arms be placed far from her sides, and bind each one with a cloth conveniently.
And then the midwife follows on the right side and administers the instrument with which the opening of the belly is made, the form of which will come in those causes that will be mentioned here.
And it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument, you should place yourself in front of the woman's belly and ensure that only the point of the instrument enters the belly and leads towards the ulcer. But if the instrument is larger than the point of the belly, then it is necessary that you place poultices on the texture of the point of the belly so that the entrance of any instrument into the point of the belly is prohibited.
And it is necessary that you place the thread which runs through the instrument on the right side above, and that the one who ministers holds the instrument and turns the thread until the opening of the belly has been made.
And when the exit comes out and is touched with the hand and is loose and moist, then it is necessary that you dry that with a broad spatula.
And when the sanies has been evacuated, then it is necessary that you place in the wound a medicated wick soaked in rose oil or green oil with some astringency; and let the compress remain on the section of the point of the belly.
And then cover the belly and place over it clean wool immersed in water in which mallows have been boiled.
"Then it should be treated for about two days until it heals."
"Sometimes the wound is washed with honey and then rinsed with water in which iris root or long pepper has been boiled, and then it is returned to the wound."
"If the wound has gone deep into the flesh, then you should forbear from treating it with iron and instead use water as we have described in this section."
"Chapter 75."
"To teach midwives how to treat women with abnormal uterine bleeding according to their figurative causes."
"It is necessary that the midwife know at the beginning the figure of a natural childbirth by its signs. When you see the woman pressing on her thighs and desiring to smell the air, and she is relieved when something comes out from her above, and hastens the expulsion of the baby, then you will know that this birth is according to nature, and it exits onto her head, and the second one with its cord either suspended or pendant from the navel."
"Therefore, when you see those signs, then the belly should be pressed so that the baby may come out easily. When it comes out onto its head, the second one follows, and is cleansed of those superfluities with good cleansing."
"But if this is not that birth, it is abnormal and blameworthy, for when the baby comes out on its feet, its body comes out before its head and its feet, and its hand is one, or at its foot, or its head comes out with its hand, or at its belly, and its face is turned upwards towards its neck, such are the figures of abnormal births."
"Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all those causes, so that she may guard against error and deception."
"And I will show you all the figures of those births, and what kind they are in them, so that it may be understood by this and judged accordingly."
"When the feet come out first due to an upright position and it is violent upon the woman, and she has a difficult delivery, and her strength is already weakened, then she should do this: women should have her sit up, and evacuate her with fennugreek decoction and olive oil."
"And then the midwife should insert her finger between the baby's thighs and tear it open with that, or separate it with her nail within what is in it of humidity." "And press on the woman's belly so that she may expel the baby."
"But if it does not come out, then the woman should be anointed with pitch and fennugreek mucilage mixed with nard."
"And then command her to be pressed down again, and make her sneeze with incense; and put your mouth and nose over hers for one hour, for the baby will soon be forgotten."
"And if both arms of the baby are forgotten at the beginning, then you should reduce them gently little by little." "But if it does not obey the intermediation, then place the woman on a large stone and lift her legs up, and quickly push the stone down towards the ground; and let the woman be held so that she does not fall due to the shock."
"And if the arms are not returned and the baby dies, then cut them open and remove the membrane of the baby or tie its body to your hand with cloth and remove it evenly, for that will soon be forgotten."
"When the baby comes out feet-first, then you should push those up, turn the baby around gently, anoint it, grasp its foot, and slowly extend it."
"But when it is already inside the uterus, then you should command it to come out, and make it sneeze with incense, for it will soon be forgotten if God wills."
"And if it is not forgotten with what we have recommended, then slowly return the baby into place according to its natural figure, for it will now be forgotten with an easy delivery."
"And if it is prohibited with all that we have recommended, then take some aloe mucilage and gum dissolved, grind them well in the mortar, and anoint the woman's belly, especially its lower part." "And then make her drink warm water to promote contractions."
"And when sometimes the parts of her are inflamed, then perform fumigation of myrtle on her and apply cold compresses." "And when fumigation has been done for an hour, then make her sit on a stone, make her sneeze and extend her mouth, lift her up, and press gently on the lower part of her belly, for the baby will soon be forgotten."
"On the emergence of the fetus lying sideways with one arm extended:" "It should be gently reduced into place by its hand. But if you cannot reduce it, then lift the woman up and make her walk."
"And if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, strike its sides with vigorous blows, and administer liquids and mucilages which you have prepared."
"And if the childbirth has come, then make her sit on a stone, study how to reduce its arm, anoint the baby according to its natural figure, make the woman sneeze, and command her to push until it is forgotten."
"On the emergence of the fetus on its back with arms extended and face towards its mother:" "The midwife should hold the baby's hand and gently turn it around until it is easy."
"And when it has been anointed and it has become easy, then place on its face what we have recommended of oil and mucilages."
"And then command her to shake it gently little by little. And when you have done this, then make her sit on a stone and let her lean over her right side, and command her to push; and make her sneeze with incense." "Preparation for the emergence of the fetus onto its side:"
"When there are horrible cries from the mother according to this manner, consider, and then cut open the second one with your nail until it is evacuated of moisture."
"And if the baby is suspended over its face and its neck, then cut open that part with a caesarean section, so that it may not be retained and die."
And then push the fetus into the parts inside that are open, and pause that which is necessary, and tell the woman to take some breaths, and he himself will come out easily, if God wills it.
Exit of twins or multiple fetuses Know that many times twins are born, and sometimes three or four, although this is rare and strange and should not happen; but there are several causes for this, not alive.
And it happens sometimes that they are multiplied, one after another, and separated by a membrane, distinguishable those inside the ligament in the navel of each one. And sometimes they come out like this as if there were only one fetus through natural easy birth, and sometimes they come out through difficult birth like we have mentioned.
And if some of them have difficulty with childbirth and arrive at what we have said about the unnatural figures, then you should take care of them as we have mentioned.
And if the midwife is skilled and does what she does with ease and skillfulness, and with patience, and follows the method according to all figures as it was prepared for her by the master bringing about health.
Remembrance of that which is formed in the matrix from embryos and miscarriages
Sometimes there are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even more than ten embryos, and it has been verified that one woman miscarried six, and another one all ten that were formed. The cause of this was made known through the measurement by the glorious wise men.
And therefore it is necessary for the midwife to know well this little figure of that which she may encounter, and thus she will be prepared for it.
Chapter LXXVI
Of the extraction of the dead fetus
When you care for the dead fetus as we have said in the division of medicine and it has not yet come out, and you wish to use an operation with the hand, then you should consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and does not have any of the accidents which could cause harm to her.
Then it is necessary for the woman to be placed on her back with her hips elevated and her head lowered inward, and her thighs raised up.
And the assistant should hold both of her knees or she should be bound in that manner on the bed so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you should moisten the mouth of the womb with oiled honey and dough made from marshmallow, fenugreek, and sesame seed.
And then the midwife should grease her hand with those oils and doughs, and then gently insert her hand into the womb, and seek out with her hand where the hooks of the fetus are located.
And the convenient places for this are: then you should consider if the fetus is prepared to come out on its head, and thus you should find the hooks in its heels or in the neck or in the mouth or in the palate or below the beard or in the clavicle or in the places near the ribs or below the hypochondria.
But if the coming out is on its buttocks, then in the perineum or in the middle of the back.
And it is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand and place the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and gently insert the hand and place the hook in one of those places which we have mentioned, until you reach the cause of the blockage.
And then pause and place another hook or the third if it is necessary, so that there may be equal attraction, and not only extension according to its nature.
And thus it should be done in all deliveries, so that the coming out of it is made easier just as it is done in teeth before their extraction.
And it is necessary that in that which is between them the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to grease some of her fingers with oil and gently insert them and rotate them where it has been retained.
Therefore if the delivery of the fetus is delayed, then the hooks should be changed to another place where it can be more easily pushed out; and do this until the whole fetus is delivered.
But if the hand is extended before the other one and it is not possible to reduce it because of the constriction of it, then cloth should be wrapped around that one; and then extract that one until the whole is delivered, and cut it either at the junction of the hand or in the elbow.
And thus you should do with the other hand and with both feet.
"If the head of the fetus is large, or obstruction occurs during delivery, or it is in the contracted pelvis, then it is necessary to introduce the said spina spatula and split the head to remove the water, or use an instrument called 'alundat'."
"And similarly if the fetus has a large head by nature: and then it is necessary to use tongs, or use an instrument called 'alundat' as we have said before; and promptly extract the bones with forceps."
"If the head is exited but stuck beneath the pubic bone, then it should be split open so that the fluid in the cavity may drain out."
"But if there is no complication and no obstruction to delivery, then you should incise the head immediately as soon as it is possible for you."
"And if the left side of the abdomen is inflamed or there is a hydrocele, then it is necessary for you to puncture that area so that the fluid may be drained."
"But if the fetus is above its own weight, then its attraction will be lighter and its direction towards the mother's mouth will be easier."
"But if it is stuck beneath the abdomen and the cavity, then you should extract it with cloth that you will have wrapped around your hand, and split open the abdomen and cavity so that water may flow out from them."
"But if the other members are out and the head turns back, then insert your left hand; but if the mother's mouth is filled, then insert your hand into the bird's throat, grasp the head with it, and pull it with those instruments into the mother's mouth, and promptly insert a hook or two hooks and pull it with them."
"And if the mother's mouth is obstructed by an abscess that has formed there, then it should not be troubled over it; but at that time it is necessary to administer evacuation of thick moist causes." "And apply plasters; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten."
"And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible it should be turned; and it should be administered as we have said for a live fetus."
"But if that is not possible, then it should be incised in pieces, and it should be extracted."
"And you must not leave any cause behind inside the uterus."
"And when you have completed all your operation, then administer as we have said for the treatment of burns that have occurred in the mother."
"And if bleeding occurs, then apply lint soaked in astringent waters and administer the other treatment."
"And I have already seen a woman whose womb contained a dead fetus, and she became pregnant again promptly thereafter, and the other fetus was also dead." "It happens that an abscess forms in the womb for a long time; it swells inside until it bursts, and it begins to discharge watery blood."
"And I was called to treat it, and I treated it for a long time, but the ulcer did not heal."
"Then I applied plasters of strong attraction for these causes, and after some days an bone came out from it, and again after a few days another bone came out. And I was greatly amazed because there are no bones in the womb."
"And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus."
"So I healed the ulcer, and extracted many bones from it, and the woman remained in her usual condition, and she lived thus for a long time with only a little discharge of watery blood."
"And I do not affirm that this is strange, but rather it shows that in this there is science and help for what the skilled physician administers with his hand by means of treatment."
"Of the shapes of the instruments necessary to extract the fetus."
"The shape of a hook with which the uterus is dilated:"

"And each rod should be two fingers wide and one finger thick at the edge of each, and each should be a hand and a half long; and in the middle of both rods there are two attachments for that same rod which are already fixed, each of which is about a hand and a few digits long, and each is two fingers or a little more wide."
"And these two attachments are inserted into the mouth of the uterus so that it may be dilated with them when you turn the two specified hooks."
"Another form similar to this, but more slender and lighter:"
"It should be made of silver or boxwood according to the shape of forceps." "But at the end of it there are two attachments like this, and each attachment is about two fingers wide."

"Of the extraction of the secondine:"
"When the secondine is retained during childbirth, then you should command the sick woman to hold her breath, and immediately make her sneeze with conditions, and stretch your hand over the mouth of it and over her nose, and if it comes out by this means, so much the better."

"Treatment for an unperforated child's buttocks."
"The child's navel and buttocks are not pierced; they are still subtle and closed." "Then tell the midwife to pierce that navel with her sharp needle; if not, pierce it with a pointed needle, taking care not to touch the skin."

"Regarding the treatment of fistulas that develop from these wounds."
"The fistulas that develop in the lower part of the buttocks are usually large and thick, those that develop near the anus outside or in the space between the two cheeks."
"And it is one fistula or several."
"And since this swelling is ancient and comes from moist, thick white humors or subtle corruption, sometimes these fistulas have some penetrating openings."
"And these openings are known through that which is issuing from them by way of exit and windiness; sometimes the patient expels it themselves, and often worms come out."
"And sometimes these fistulas enter into the urinary bladder through those penetrating openings, and also into the flesh of the penis; and some of these openings extend to the junction of the thighs and into the groin."
"And the way to recognize a penetrating fistula entering the anus and not visible from the outside is by placing your little finger inside the anus and then probing gently with a fine thread of silk or iron until you reach the fistula."
"But if there is tortuosity (twisting) in that direction, then insert a fine thread of lead or horsehair into the fistula until you feel it brush against your little finger."
"And if you do not feel it at all nor perceive any cause of expulsion, worms, or windiness as we have said before, then you will know that the fistula is not penetrating, and therefore you can proceed to its treatment."
"And when the fistula penetrates into the bladder or into the flesh of the penis, then its significance is urinary leakage from that area, and prohibition of its use until the place is healed as it should be according to medical practice."
"But if it penetrates into the junction of the thighs or into the bone and its surroundings with pain in the affected area, then the sign is that the probe passes through there if there is no tortuosity within the bone, and pain at the outset; and that pus always issues from there, and that nothing helps, nor does it heal with ointments."
"And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no complete cure, and the cure of those is a matter of discussion among foolish physicians on which we do not stand firm."
"But in that one which is not penetrating and is not ancient, healing with iron is expected as I will recommend to you, and what I have already said."
"And the disease causes pain between his buttocks, more particularly on the left side and elevates the cheeks of the buttocks, with the thighs inclined towards the belly of the patient. Then insert a probe of lead or iron if there is tortuosity in the fistula until you know where it passes."
"And if that person feels pain around the anus, then you should insert your little finger into the anus."
If you feel the tent through your finger and it is already exposed penetrating, or if you feel something between your finger and that flesh, then certainly know that it has penetrated; and therefore do not work on that, for it is not in that area.
However, some say that it is healthy in some men to be hard-hearted.
And the treatment by which it is hoped that the patient will be benefited is this: you kindle a cautery with great subtlety according to the width of the fistula, as was previously described, and insert that burning iron into the fistula until it reaches around the buttocks; and apply it again two or three times until you know that all those flesh joined by the fistula are already burnt, like the feathers of a bird's quill.
And then dress that with wet bandages wrapped in wool until all those burnt flesh are healed, and afterwards dress it with medicines that generate and consolidate flesh, and if it is healed, good. But if not, then it will never be healed by any other treatment at any time.
And if the probe enters but does not penetrate within the depth of the said buttock, and there is some space between that and the probe which is wrapped in flesh or cloth, then open the fistula where its surface is level with the spine, and cut off the skin at the beginning of the fistula, and insert the probe into the fistula until the incision reaches to the place where the end of the probe arrives; and through the probe it will be freed and cured.
And then clean those flesh joined by the fistula which are like bird's feather quills, so that they do not break off for any reason.
But if blood often flows between you and your operation when you touch those flesh, then it is a wound, and it should be cauterized with fire or with sharp medicine, for cauterizing with fire is suitable for two habits: it joins those joined flesh together and cuts off the blood and dries out the moisture.
And then dress it with wet bandages wrapped in wool or cloth until the place gets warm; and then cure the wound with medicines that generate and consolidate hard flesh.
And those medicines are astringent and drying; when it is restored, then it will be healed and there will be no recurrence.
"However, if the fistula has already penetrated into the anus and extends beyond its surface, then insert your finger into the anus and explore with it."
"If you find the vessel, and between it and the rectum there is nothing but skin or flesh, and it is close to penetration, then do not operate on it, but rather through faith and hope."
"There are three ways to manage this: either cauterize it as we have said; or cut into it until you achieve the concavity that allows you to enter the parts and facilitate healing; but do not proceed with cutting unless necessary so as not to damage the contents of the rectum, and so that you do not incur blame for acting against nature's will. Rather, treat it with what we have said if you want a speedy recovery. Or else extend this membrane and cleanse the pus from within the perineum, as we have said, either with a probe or another instrument with a sharp tip; then thoroughly wash these fistulous tissues which are in the sectioned area using a cauterizing method; finally strive to restore all the parts that were cut away." "And when the fistula is seen to be finished in this manner: namely, when you insert the probe into the fistula and it emerges from the surface of the skin around the anus or at the margin of the buttocks, then take a probe with a perforated tip, which is shaped like a needle for preparing hearts thus:"
"And insert it into that opening wrapped in linen or cotton, and then insert the probe with the filament into the fistula until you achieve its concavity."
"But if it is penetrating into the margin of the anus from behind, then remove the filament from that passage so that you can insert your probe as described earlier. Then extract the tip of the filament and tie the two ends together with a knot; twist each end separately; leave this for one or two days; and when you have incised the skin around it, cleanse it thoroughly so that those tissues which are between the two ends of the filament become exposed."
"And then heal the wound until it is consolidated and healed."
"But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in whatever way you have prepared yourself, but do so gently, for it is not your task to cause injury to the skin. And then treat it until it is healed."
"The shape of the spatha spinos used to incise the fistula is such that one end is very sharp and the other end is not sharp. This way you will not cut unnecessarily as often happens."
"Regarding the suture of hemorrhoids in which blood flows from the incision of those (hemorrhoids):"
"Hemorrhoids occur in two ways: either they are between the buttocks resembling coal or they appear like growths of fat." "And those are small and large, from which blood always flows and is one, and there are many, and they are outside the anus, and at its extremities."
"But those that are outside the anus occur more often in those with little humidity, from which citrine water or a bit of blood continuously flows, and they vary in color."
"And the treatment for those inside the anus is to command the patient to sit and squeeze while they exhale, so that the anus opens and the hemorrhoids appear." "Then you grasp with tweezers or your nail and squeeze those hard ones close to their roots."
"But if the tweezers do not hold those hard ones due to their humidity and softness, then take them with rough cloth or cotton or wool wadding, squeeze them with your fingers, cut them close to their roots, and apply some powdered myrrh near the incision, so that they are cauterized in place. Or else cauterize them as it was said in the chapter on cauterization." "And then treat those with the other cure until they are healed."
"And if the anus does not obey to evacuation, then cauterize the patient with a cautery having a small bite, and wash it with water that is in the anus so that it may evacuate easily when the patient squeezes."
"But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, their cause is slight, and it suffices for you to grasp them with your nail or tweezers, cut them, and then treat them with water as we have said until they are healed."
"And if you make an incision, then administer sutures in this manner: take a thread and insert it into a needle and then pull the hemorrhoid out on both sides. Then make the needle penetrate into the root of the other side, and wrap the two ends of the thread around the part that is far from the needle, and do this crosswise. Then tie the hemorrhoid tightly with the thread, and cut off the excess thread."
"And do this to all of them, leaving one alone without tying it, so that the superfluous blood may flow out from that one."
"And then put a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the anus, and put another one on the buttocks. Then command the patient to remain quiet." "And then leave that one inside until it falls off; and when it has fallen off, treat it with ointment or with another cure until it is healed."
"And since those are old and not useful for this medicine, it is necessary that you remove them with the point of a scalpel or with your nail until they are moistened and covered by pus on top, which prevents their consolidation; and thus cure those that have already consolidated."
"Then you remove them with a vehement scraping until the first blood appears and they are scraped clean; and thus cure those that have healed."
"Know that hemorrhoids, which are called the key of disease, are not round like the head of a nail, but they are found throughout the body and especially in those parts near the buttocks and rectum. And it is through these that you should examine them."
"And then it is necessary that what is in the circuit of the key be incised and held with forceps or a hook, and completely eradicated from its root; and thus cure it."
"If you wish, cauterize the second one that is mentioned in its chapter."
"But a verruca is a small, rough, flesh-colored bump with a round base that appears on the surface of the body, and many are found in children."
"The treatment for it [a verruca] is to stretch out and incise that [the verruca], or remove it with a file or a scalpel until it bleeds." "And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or with an acute medicine, as we have said."
"But a formica [wart] is a small, flat or fistulated bump on the surface of the body that appears frequently on the face. When it is touched, it feels like an ant bite and is found throughout the body."
"The treatment for it [a wart] is to take a quill from an owl or a vulture feather, and it should be thick. Place the quill on the wart so that its tip contains thewart within its circle; then rotate your hand with the quill so that you incise what is in the circuit of the wart, and press down on the skin around it, and thus eradicate the root of the wart."
"And if you wish, do this with a cautery needle or iron according to this method:"
"That the tip of the needle should be thin and blunt (i.e. not perforated), wrapped in such a way that when it is placed on the said part, its edge is sharpened and its rotation made easier."
"And if you wish to cauterize the wart according to what was mentioned earlier in the chapter on cautery regarding anthrax."
"Regarding the forms of instruments used for giving cautery."
"Sometimes cautery is done with silver or lead or melted wax or dough. And sometimes it is done with those instruments which are small or large according to those that are used, for the one used in treating young children should be small; and those whose handles are curved or elongated, their cauteries should be small."
"The method of cautery that is large and rare:"
"That the head of the cautery needle above which the bag is tied should be wide in this manner, and that at its distinction where the bag is tied it should be like this."
"And the lower extremity of it which is inserted into the bag should be blunt (i.e. not open) and thickened towards subtlety; and on one side of it there are two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the rays, i.e. the larger the ray, the wider the hole."
"And let the bag in which the medicines of bladder or sheep's wool are placed be one palm long."
"And it should be pierced with many holes around it, the space between which is equal to the thickness of the finger."
"And then insert into those holes strong boiling oil of unripe olives, or pour it around them. Then adjust the bag onto it [the cautery needle]; and when the bag is placed on it, tighten it at the head of the cautery between two distinctions with a strong constriction, and then cauterize each hole: But be careful to not let the medicine in the bag become too hot or too cold."
"And then the patient should lie on his back, elevate his buttocks, and place beneath them a cloth upon which he may rest or a towel. Then anoint the extremity of the cautery with oil or albumen of egg or mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances; then insert it into the bag easily, and then the assistant should take the bag and squeeze it with two hands repeatedly with vigor until all that is in the cautery is expelled into the bowl. Then remove the cautery and the patient should raise his buttocks against the wall."
"And if the medicine forces it out to emission, let him hold it thus until he can no longer. And if he sleeps with it overnight, it is more beneficial."
"But if you cauterize him in cases of loose bowels and emission of feces from the anus, then repeat the cautery until he is healed."
"And if there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then use a thin and thick cautery needle like those used for children."
"On the treatment of plague:"
"And I have already mentioned in the section on the treatment of plague what was appropriate for this book, and now I will say how those who are sick with it should be treated with medicine according to the complete regimen."
"I say that plague is differentiated according to what kind of plague is present and according to the place where the plague strikes."
"And the causes for which plague often occurs are such as: cutting with a sword or knife, piercing with a dart or scissors, striking with a lance or club or arrow, and similar things caused by many causes."
"But plague that occurs in the parts of the body is such as: plague that falls upon the head, neck, chest, abdomen, thigh, and similar things on the members."
"And I am recounting the treatment of certain plague wounds because this reasoning and rule may also be applied to other kinds of plague wounds."
"And I will begin with simple head plague wounds, because the memory of compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter."
"I say that when a simple head wound occurs and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it was caused by a blow from a sword or similar thing, and the chain has been broken only on one side and it is a large wound and you fear that an abscess may follow, then promptly perform a cephalic incision and flebotomy on him and do not delay this; and draw out from him as much blood as possible according to the amount of its strength if there is no other cause prohibiting flebotomy, especially if the blood which has issued from the wound is little."
"And let the flebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part, and keep the patient from sneezing, drinking wine, and eating heavy foods."
"But if you prohibit some cause because of its minuteness, then let him be weakened in his diet and not approach meat or wine."
"And if an abscess follows upon the wound, then cut into it with oil boiled rose oil or with wine in which has been steeped."
"If you are certain of an abscess, then place a poultice on it, if it is fresh with its own blood and the air has not yet changed there around the powder which I will recommend shortly."
"And if the air has already changed there, then place a poultice on it until it is healed."
"However, if the wound is large or due to an incision and its edges are not aligned properly because of dust, then approximate those edges with stitches according to my instructions on wound closure."
"If the wound is already exposed to the bone and there's no retention of it but only a small suspension, then incise that area and properly cure the wound with medications. Restore the flesh appropriately in place of the cord. And command the patient to be fed on foods which are coarse: heads and entrails and similar things, until they recover."
"If you find putrefaction in the cord and it does not adhere to the bone, then incise all that is purulent and remove it. And properly cure it."
"But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flow can occur and it is not severed by medications, then inquire about the artery. And if you find that one not incised, then incise it with a scalpel, or ligate it. And if necessity compels you to do otherwise than what has been said, then cauterize until the bleeding stops."
"And if these wounds are simple and small, then their cause is light. Therefore, you powder those with this powder, because they will consolidate before the air can change them."
"And the manner of making this powder is as follows: Take oil of sesame one part, blood of dragon's blood two parts, and resin of mastic three parts. All of it should be finely ground and sieved. Then fill the wound with it, and constrict it well so that it adheres to it, and coagulate it with the blood."
"And properly constrain that above with powders and let it be. And do not remove it while it is like this until it is well adhered, because the medicine will not desert it until it is healed."
"And sometimes you can use cautery alone when sesame oil and dragon's blood are not available."
"And this same operation is performed on large wounds when it is necessary to cover those with it and constrain them tightly. And these are fresh wounds with their own blood, which the air has not altered."
"And if the air has altered them, and especially during summer time, then this powder is not intended for those wounds. But at that time treat those with what has been said above, such as applying these ointments: a mixture of white lead and olive oil, or flour paste with water and honey until they gain consistency; and properly treat those with the other remedies until they are healed."
"But if there is a fracture of bone in the wound and it is small, then remove that with a gesture (i.e., manipulation)."
"And I say here the treatment of fractures of the head as it is venomous."
"Regarding wounds of the neck:"
"But if the wound is on the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple head wound."
"But if the nerve or artery of the neck is cut, then if it is a nerve, there is nothing to do but avoid treating it with anything that causes violent contraction, such as vitriol and similar things which cause pain to nerves. It contracts." "And do not apply any ointment to the wound because the substance of nerves is fatty and their continuity is with the brain, which is the father of all members."
"And if you treat it with light remedies like this: washing the wound with sweet water, sometimes infused in white or unrefined oil, and turpentine when washed with sweet water; and other minor remedies according to this manner, and moist ointments."
"But if the wound is large, then apply sutures or tie the lips of it, and properly treat it with powders until it is healed."
"But if the wound has depth or the bone at its bottom is broken into pieces, then make a hole in it at the lowest point."
"But if an artery is cut in the wound and there is bleeding, then separate or dry that, or ligate it, or cauterize it if necessary."
"But if the cervical vertebrae or all of them have been injured but the veins of the neck are saved, then adjust the lips of the wound with sutures over the windpipe and do not touch it; bind it evenly and reduce it to its natural figure, and properly treat it with bandages decently stretched, leaving it for some days; and properly treat it with ointments that have astringent and stimulating properties until it is healed."
"But if the wound goes deeply into the bone and causes inflammation there, then percuss it. And if there are fragments of bone there, remove all those that you can; and what cannot be removed, leave it until the wound becomes suppurated, separated, and its inflammation is relieved."
"And if the wound is fresh, then powder it with that powder which I have recommended to you." "But if there is a fistulous wound in the wound, then treat it with that of which I will remind you properly in its chapter."
"If it is a wound made by a sword or knife and its depth varies, then consider whether wind escapes from the wound when breathing; if it does, know that the wound is mortal."
"And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with its blood, then put on it at first hour powder, but do not bind it so that the blood does not remain in the depth of it and return to the heart, aggravating the condition; rather put on a moist attractive ointment and wash it twice a day."
"And if the ointment is not available, then put cotton wool on the mouth of the wound so that it sucks what comes from the humidities; and make sure the patient sleeps over the wound so that what is collected there runs."
"But if three days or more have passed since the wound and there is no spasm nor heart failure nor respiratory difficulty in the patient, and other dispositions are good for him, know that the wound is saved. Then treat it with bandages and other remedies until it is healed."
"But if the healing of it is delayed and much time has passed, know that a fistulous wound has already formed. Then treat it according to its chapter."
"And if the wound is made by a slash or knife and is simple on the surface of the flesh or back, then treat it with what has been mentioned about sutures if it is large, or powder if it is small."
"But if inflammation has already occurred in the bone and pieces of it have been cut off, then twist the wound and try to extract those pieces if they are separated." "But if they are not separated, then leave them until the wound becomes suppurated, as their extraction will be easier then."
"And regarding other accidental wounds in the other members, the remedy in treatment is the same as what we have said."
"Regarding abdominal wounds."
"The condition that occurs in the belly may be great, small, or moderate."
"And a small rupture is difficult to repair by another method, and so its reduction is more difficult if you don't promptly perform its insertion back into its place, because if it breaks open and becomes swollen then its reinsertion is made difficult."
"And therefore the best rupture is moderate, because in that case it is not difficult to reduce the hernia, as is difficult in both kinds mentioned before."
"And you should know that there are four ways to suture the belly, but two of these sutures are common and suitable for the suturing of other wounds on the body."
"And the other two sutures are more specific to the belly wound, although they can also be used for other wounds."
"And I recommend to you each one with its exposition and explanation."
"Therefore I say that when the wound is small and some cause of the hernia has come out through it, and it is difficult to reduce it, there are two ways to do this: either because of the smallness of the rupture, as we have said, or because the intestine has become inflamed due to the cold air."
"And therefore, when it is like this, you should then make an incision so that you submerge a sponge or cloth dampened in warm water alone, or with vinegar, celery seed, and spice, and dress the hernia with it until the inflammation has been resolved."
"And sometimes do this with wine in which there is astringency, and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflammation."
"And therefore, when you see that the inflammation has been resolved, then you moisten the hernia with water in which marshmallow and mallows have been cooked, because this relieves the pain without much cause."
"But if the pain has not been relieved by this treatment, then cut the rupture a little with an instrument with which you have previously cauterized hemorrhoids."
"And the first treatment is better when it is proper that it not be cut, and there is no need to cut except in necessity and deficiency."
"What about the instrument? Describe its shape:"
"One part of it is cut sharp and the other not-sharp, with a pointed tip that is not too fine like a scalpel, rather it should be somewhat blunt."
"And therefore, when the wound has widened and the hernia has come out, then its reduction should be according to its natural form, in its proper place if possible, for this is better."
"But when the rupture is wide and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, then you should make the patient lie on his back and elevate his hips as much as his head; but if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then elevate the head of the bed and raise the feet as much as possible."
"And similarly, if the rupture is in one of the two sides of the abdomen, then always place your intention and consideration there so that the side in which the wound is may be higher than the other."
"And this should be done for both large and medium-sized wounds."
"And in small wounds, do what you have prepared for it, but especially make sure that the one who ministers is among your closest associates, who holds the rupture entirely with his hand and adjusts the lips of it, and especially uncover from that to this so that the suturing may be done without any other cause."
"And this is the common method of suturing: first take the needle, or count needles according to the amount of the width of the wound; and then leave it at the end of the index finger, and thread the needle with one thread, but do not put a knot in both ends of the string, with two threads of the gut that is on the left side of the string, so that you make this penetrate from there into that part; and now you have four orders."
"And then thread with doubled gut around the needle, and sometimes thread two parts together, and then attach both lips and the wound decently by suturing; and then leave the thickness of your finger and insert another needle there, and then tie it with gut like the first one with its needle; and do not stop doing this until you have completed all the contraction of the wound."
"And let the needles be medium in thickness and subtlety, for thin needles cut too easily into the flesh, and thick ones are difficult to insert into the gut; therefore they should be medium in both thickness and subtlety."
"And it is not necessary to insert the needle into both ends of the gut at once, for if the flesh is cut too easily and the wound opens before its consolidation."
"And do not prolong the suturing so that the wound may not be hindered from consolidation."
"And then cut off the ends of the needles so that the patient may not be disturbed while sleeping; and then place over the suturing powdered breadcrumbs on both sides, which will hold the ends of the needles; and leave them there until you know that the wound is consolidated."
"And these kinds of suturing with needles are more convenient for small wounds, for it is enough to suture them with one needle or two or around those."
"But the second kind of suturing is common: it is that you suture the four ends of the gut and both ends of the gut in one go with a needle which has gut wound around it in subtlety and thickness."
"And then when the needle has penetrated these four ends, reduce the needle from that same part where you began, so that the gut may draw up from the most elevated part of the wound, so that the suturing is like sewing with cloth, in which the threads are drawn tight."
"And place between each suture the thickness of your little finger."
"And this suturing is known to men."
"And with this suturing, I closed a wound that had been accidentally inflicted on a man in his belly who had been stabbed with a knife, and the disruption of the wound was more than a palm wide, and it was issuing from the bowels around two palms of the bowel near the middle, and the disruption was in the middle of the member; and then I reduced it after the bowel had been forced out by the wound for twenty-four hours."
"And the wound was consolidated in the space of fifteen days or thereabouts, and I cured that man and he is healed; and even now he lives many years after, and is well disposed in his affairs."
"And the other physicians had judged that he would not be healed; and by a miracle he was healed, for I did not cure him with any ointment, for it was in a place where no ointment could be applied nor any medicine, but I put upon the wound cotton dipped twice a day in honey water until he was healed."
"But I will tell two kinds of suturing proper according to the narrative of the Word."
"And it is that you begin with the suturing of the gut, and enter the needle from without to within."
When the needle enters the spine and that joint, following the straightness and length of the entire body, leaving the end of the needle in what has been pierced; then make the needle enter from inside to outside on the other end of the muscle.
And then when you have made it penetrate once, then make it penetrate again in that same joint of the muscle from outside to inside; and leave the end of the needle that is on this side, and make the needle penetrate into the other end from inside to outside.
And then with that penetration where you make it penetrate into the needle at the end of the muscle which is on the inside, everything should penetrate.
And moreover, start from this same side and pull that with the end which is of the needle on the other side, and remove the needle from the spine which has penetrated, and then put it back into that spine and join the end of the needle which is on the other side with this end of the muscle; and remove that needle from the spine which is on the other side.
And do this once and again, and do it once more with one more stroke inside that you consider everything is done according to that example.
And the sum of this manner of suturing is that you should use skin sutures with which to sew the skin, in such a way that you sew the needle once from the side of the spine's end, and then leave it inside until you have completed it.
Moreover, the second type of suturing which is specifically mentioned by Guy de Chauliac, and this concerns only the muscle and its recommendation is that you sew it in half with the aid of some medicine, so that each part adheres to its corresponding part according to nature; and they apply the end of one side to the other end of the muscle, and that is done according to what I recommend to you.
You should leave the needle in the end of the muscle near the defect and make it penetrate into the interior of that part, leaving both ends of the needle outside; then turn the needle around and make it penetrate from outside to inside through both ends of the muscle.
And then turn those loops again, and make each loop penetrate from inside the interior part to outside the exterior part on both ends of the muscle except for that which is on the opposite side.
And this manner of suturing is better than common light suturing, and it is the type of suturing which I have previously mentioned.
This is what Guy de Chauliac said
Moreover, some say that abdominal suturing is corrected with two needles, so you should insert a thread into these loops and begin with the needle insertion from where it is necessary for you to do so, and make it penetrate inside the other side according to the suturing of those who sew the intestines equally.
And know that when there is a rupture in the middle of the abdomen, abdominal suturing at that point is more difficult than elsewhere on the abdomen.
But the treatment of plague is judged by other plagues.
Which means that when you encounter fresh plague with its own blood before the air alters it, and reduce the wound and sew it up and dress it properly, then you apply powder of cinnabar on it.
And if the air has already altered the plague, then you apply to it some ointments which are present at that time before they make a hard crust and draw out the threads, and let them be consolidated both inside and outside; and then cure it like other wounds until it is healed.
But if you do not have medicines present at that time, then apply something to it immediately, for it begins to emit bad smell and soon changes color twice a day, as I have shown you, until it is healed, because you will not need other medications in many cases when the plague is simple.
But if you fear that the plague may communicate to the main limbs, then you should submerge lion's wool in good quality olive oil or rose oil and apply it around the area between the anus and leave it there.
And if there is pain or putrefaction in its bowels, which happens many times, then you should crystallize it with black treacle and vinegar, especially if the putrefaction has reached the bowel and an exiting wound has been made penetrating into its concavity.
And know that those which are in the large intestine have easier healing than those which are in the small intestines.
And it is difficult to heal that intestine which is called "gizzard" because it does not receive healing of plague that enters into it at all; and this is because of the great multitude of veins that are in it, and its great magnitude, and its subtlety of its body, and its proximity to the nature of nerves.
But if what proceeds from the plague is tissue, and you encounter it fresh, then reduce it according to your discretion with which you reduce intestines equally.
But if it has passed some time and it has become green or black, then stretch it with thread over the location that is discolored from it, so that there comes out flow of blood, because in the tissue there are veins and arteries.
And then incise that which is other than that thread and leave two ends of the thread pendant from the opening outside the plague so that you may be relieved of the attraction of it, because of the closing of the tissue and emission of the smell of the plague.
Reminder about plague when it occurs in the bowel.
When rupture occurs in the intestine and is severe, it may be possible to restore it in some men.
Therefore I pursued the treatment of him as if he were not destined to be cured, but rather to subtiliate that wound which had been healed and the place was consolidated.
And I saw that the place was consolidated, therefore I advised him to pay attention to his health after this misfortune in his belly; and not to become too careless with his meals and drinks, but rather to enter between baths and exercise himself in his customs.
And some experienced ones have said that when rupture occurs in the intestine and is severe, it is necessary to tie it according to this manner: take frogs with large heads; then adjust the two lips of the rupture and place one frog of those that have their mouth open on the two lips of the rupture; therefore when it presses on them and tightens its mouth, cut off its head because it adheres and is not dissolved.
And also place another frog near the first one, and do not cease doing this until you have used as many frogs as there is length of the rupture.
And then reduce it and close the rupture; those attached heads will remain in the intestine until the intestine is healed, without causing any harm to the patient.
And it is also possible to tie the intestine with a fine thread made from the gut of an animal, because it is more suitable for this purpose. Take the end of such threads and remove as much fat as possible; then tie the end of it with the thread in a loop knot, and insert that thread through a needle and sew up the intestine at the rupture, reducing it there.
And this method of suturing with frogs is merely a matter of faith and hope.
But if the rupture is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the small intestines, because then it does not result in mere suturing but rather in merely a narrowing, and not a healing of the entire intestine.
Of the treatment of wounds and fistulas
Know that every rupture or abscess when it becomes hollowed out and ancient, and is not consolidated and continually discharges pus without being cut open, then in whatever limb it may be, it is universally called a fistula, and we call it that wound.
And truly speaking, a fistula is a hard and rough nodule that is white in color and does not cause pain or discomfort, just like the concavity of the claw of an owl; therefore it was named "alcus rictus", which means "penis".
And in moist ulcers there is discharge of pus; but soon after the moisture is cut off, it becomes dry. Sometimes this moisture is abundant, sometimes scarce and thick or thin.
"All these causes have been explained, along with their symptoms and the treatments for them in the division [of medicine]."
"And it is also necessary that I inform you about the treatment of fistulas, which is performed through surgery using a scalpel."
"And you should know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body. Some are related to large veins and arteries, others to nerves, the bladder, or some of the ribs, or certain vertebrae of the back, or certain joints composed by composition like those of the hand and foot; and there are also those that arise near the main member and similar ones."
"And therefore, among these fistulas, those that are difficult to heal and do not receive treatment are considered incurable. They are caused by carelessness, ignorance, and negligence."
"And if there is any fistula whose depth does not reach those places that have been mentioned, and you hope to heal it but are uncertain about its treatment, then take a probe made of lead or iron, and if the fistula runs straight, examine it with that."
"But if the fistula is tortuous, then examine it with a probe made of thin lead, because lead due to its weight will bend and follow the twists."
"And if the fistula emits horrible sounds, it is not possible for you to examine it with a probe."
"Therefore, relieve the horrific sounds with your sounds, because the moisture that you use to rinse it will also go down the other openings and channels."
"And properly inquire and examine to determine whether you have touched the ear or nerve, whether the fistula is long or short, whether it has many openings with horrible sounds that are all covered by the skin of its entire surface. "Concerning the treatment of sinus and the quality of cleansing with medicines."

"Arrow extraction."
"Arrows vary according to species and the body locations they target. Their diversity lies in having large, small, concave, blunt, or solid points. Some have three edges, others tongues, while still others are star-shaped."
"If the arrow strikes the brain and pierces the skull, causing damage to the cerebrum above it, symptoms may include sudden violent headache, scotoma (partial loss of vision), vertigo (dizziness), ringing in the ears, inflammation and redness of the eyelids, confusion or mixture of thoughts, vomiting bile, difficulty speaking with possible loss of speech, and leakage of watery, whitish fluid resembling flour from the wound site, accompanied by excessive moisture similar to that of flesh."
"Therefore, if these symptoms are apparent, it is advisable to abstain from attempting to treat the wound or remove the arrow unless it is protruding outside."
"If the arrow strikes near the left nipple and is deeply embedded in hard tissue (not soft), with movement of the arrowhead resembling a heartbeat, accompanied by bleeding of dark blood from the wound site, coldness or numbness in the extremities, profuse sweating, paleness, and syncope (fainting), then know that death will soon ensue without delay."
"If the arrow wounds the lung, there will be frothy bloody sputum from the wound site, coughing or choking near the collar area, change in the patient's complexion, rapid breathing, shortness of breath, and urgent desire for cold air."
"If the arrow strikes the diaphragm (velum), located in the lower chest area, there will be pain near the lower ribs, and accompanied by rapid breathing with intense pain and sighing. All movements of the muscles of the limbs are weakened."
"If the arrow strikes the stomach, there will be vomiting of undigested food from the wound site."
"If the arrow strikes the abdomen and is embedded within it, there will be a visible wound or tear in the skin, tissue, or bowel which has been ruptured. There is little hope for recovery with such an injury, as extraction of the arrow would be futile."
"If the arrow strikes the bladder and urine is expelled from the wound site, or if there are other signs of injury to external parts nearby, accompanied by intense pain over the affected area, then know that this is a fatal injury."
"However, other areas such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, arms, and joints of the backbone, collarbone, and sternum are considered safe provided that the arrow does not strike a vein or artery and is not poisonous."
"And I advise you to consider this information about arrows for your own use in treating such injuries."
"Why is it that when an arrow struck the tear duct of a man's eye during battle, I removed it from the other side near his ear and the wound healed without causing any damage to his eye?"
"And when I extracted another arrow that had struck a Jew in the socket of his eye, leaving the eyelid intact and then partially closing it, I could not find the arrowhead as it was already concealed. All that remained was a small extremity attached to his cheekbone, and it was a large, sharp Turkish arrow with a lion-shaped tip that had no barbs."
"And the Jew survived, without injury to his eye despite this serious wound."

"And I extracted another arrow from a man who had been struck in the abdomen and believed he would die from this wound. However, after thirty days with no change in his condition or signs of improvement, I made an incision over the arrow and carefully removed it, allowing him to recover without further injury."
"I once saw a man in whom an arrow had become embedded in his back. The wound became consolidated over time and remained there for about seventy years, until it eventually emerged near the sternum."
"I saw a woman in whom an arrow had become embedded in her abdomen. The wound became consolidated within her and did not change her physical condition in any way; she suffered no injury to her natural functions."
"I saw another man in whom an arrow had become lodged in his face and consolidated. The arrowhead broke off, causing him little pain, but leaving him with many scars like these."

"And I was summoned to treat him shortly after he received the wound, just three days later."
"And so I first probed the wound from the arrow quite narrowly. Then I carefully felt around with my finger but could not detect anything. But he himself felt a pricking sensation just beyond his right ear, and I suspected that this was due to the tip of the arrow."
"I then widened the wound using an instrument with which I could attract and digest matter, believing that this would help me locate the arrowhead so that it could be extracted."
"But I did not cause any significant injury to the wound despite having reached the arrowhead. I continued using the instrument for many days without causing any further harm, and meanwhile the wound had healed over. Then one day he felt the arrow inside his nose and reminded me of this."

Finally, one day I managed to grasp it with forceps designed for downward extraction and pull it out. Then I restored the wound."
"Some physicians judged that the cartilage of his nose could not be restored, but I was able to restore it and the wound healed completely. He regained his health entirely without any further complications."

"On flebotomy of veins."
The veins of phlebotomy, customarily opened for phlebotomy, are thirty in number. Among them, sixteen are on the head. There are two pulsating veins near the ears, called auricularis by some. Two veins are in the temples that appear to be twins; two veins are in the lacrimal ducts of both eyes, called aspicientia; and one vein prepared at the middle point of the forehead, and one vein at the tip of the nose; two veins at the throat; two veins on the upper lip; two veins on the lower lip; these are called algelic; and there are two veins behind the tongue. The veins that are opened for phlebotomy in the arms are five. Among them, one is cephalic and runs on the outer side of the forearm; it is called "the vein of the head" by the people. It is also a median vein composed of one branch of the basilica and another branch of the cephalic. The people name that vein "vena de tot le cors". Basilica is the vein located on the inner side of the forearm, called "citillar", or "vena del ventre" in common speech. The veins of the arm are three: the one placed above the elbow, which is opened for phlebotomy and appears clearly at the pulse; and the salvatella, which lies between the little finger and the ring finger, having two branches.
And in the thigh and leg there are three veins. One of them is located near the curvature of the little toe on the outer side of the thigh; another one is called sophena, whose location is behind the knee on the inner side of the thigh; and the third vein is sciatica, found behind the knee on the outer side of the thigh. There are other veins in the leg that resemble those mentioned above.
The veins near the ears have been found useful for treating ancient diseases such as catarrh (sinus congestion), migraines, and skin conditions like eczema and ulcers on the head.
The method of bleeding these veins is as follows:
Approach and take the lancet knife, which is pointed, and then insert it into the vein in the elbow before the phlebotomy comes to the bone. Then raise your hand gently over the vein and arm at its divisions, and cut into the vein with an incising incision. Make the length of the incision about two fingers wide or thereabouts, and let as much blood flow out as you wish.
Then press with a powder and bandage that area until it is healed
